The original letter is reproduced below: To whom it may concern, according to the letters from the delegation of overseas Chinese petitioners in Siam, the Siamese government has promulgated compulsory education and immigration laws, as well as various regulations for the management of industry and commerce. On one hand, it is implementing its assimilation policy, and on the other hand, it is restricting our country's immigrants and destroying overseas Chinese industry and commerce. Its treachery and cruelty have reached their peak. If these policies are fully implemented, our three million overseas Chinese will become slaves of Siam. Currently, the industrial, commercial, and academic circles in Siam are extremely indignant at the Siamese government's absurd measures. Although representatives have been sent to the government to argue their case, the government has ignored them due to the lack of diplomatic relations between the two countries. As a last resort, representatives have been sent back to the country to petition the government and demand strict negotiations. However, this matter has a significant impact on the future of overseas Chinese and even the nation. We earnestly request your support so that we can draw the attention of both the authorities and the public to abolish these harsh regulations and establish friendly diplomatic relations between China and Siam. It is reported that there are tens of millions of overseas Chinese in our country, and the overseas Chinese in Siam account for one-third of them. Because there are no formal diplomatic relations between China and Siam, the Siamese government is allowed to destroy and oppress them and act arbitrarily. These new regulations are particularly fatal to overseas Chinese. If we sit idly by and do nothing, not only will three million overseas Chinese be reduced to foreigners, but other countries will also follow suit, and overseas Chinese will never be guaranteed peace and security, and our country will lose its dignity as an independent country. The Association, mindful of the past, is determined to do its best to assist the request made by the overseas Chinese representatives from Siam. However, this matter is of great importance. In order to gather ideas and benefit from collective wisdom, we are forwarding this matter to your association and ask for your cooperation and assistance and to propose response measures to awaken the public and promote strict government negotiations so as to achieve the goal.

Kong Xiangrong Discusses; The Guantai Project is Extremely Consolidated; Yu Xuezhong Sends a Telegram of Gratitude 116

The Yellow River Guantai project has been completed, and the diversion of water has been successfully achieved. Director Kong Xiangrong came to Shanghai to report on the progress of the project. As reported in previous newspapers, a Central News Agency reporter visited Mr. Kong yesterday morning to learn that the Engineering Relief Group paid unusual attention to the Guantai project. The east and west main dams, side dams, and earth retaining structures have all been built to the same height as the top of the dams. On the river side, in addition to willow and stone beds, stones have been thrown to form slopes. The earth embankments connecting the two dams have been heightened and thickened and have protective eaves. They are extremely consolidated. Furthermore, on the back river side of the joint, the east and west dams in Shandong have been rooted to build enclosures, which have been completed in three days and three nights. This is called a semi-dam in Western law, which balances the water level and uses the power of water to further consolidate the new blocking project. In addition, a levee of more than six li has been built near the Longmenkou, starting from the eastern dam, and protective eaves have been added, directly reaching the Huayang levee, connecting it as one to prevent changes in the water flow. At places where the tail of the eastern dam may have backflow erosion, and with a large number of existing materials, worth about 100,000, they are used for flood protection. It seems that such repair and prevention are both extremely thorough. It is the people's fortune. Furthermore, according to Director Kong, the large amount of stone materials used for this project was purchased by the Railway Bureau. Straw, willow branches, and blue bricks were purchased by various counties. Ships and vehicles were also hired by various counties, and the material prices and transportation costs were paid in cash without any delays. Lead wire and sack were either entrusted to the association or handled by the group, and all transactions were made in cash. The personnel handling the purchases and payments were all signed and sealed to clarify responsibilities. It has been reported that there have been delays in the payment of wages. This occurred during the Guantai project undertaken by the Hebei River Affairs Bureau before the group took over. When the group took over, it was announced that the various payments owed during Director Hua's tenure should be settled by himself. It has been reported to the association that this has nothing to do with the Engineering Relief Group. This is specifically stated to avoid misunderstandings. He also disclosed the telegram received by the Huangzai Association from Chairman Yu of Hebei yesterday. It can be seen that the group's handling of the project is extremely fast, and the payment of wages is especially clear, which is admirable and respectable. Yesterday was the 34th birthday of the Japanese Emperor. Since the bombing incident two years ago, the Japanese Public Concession in Shanghai has abolished the grand celebration. This year, the celebration was held as usual. Starting at 10:00 a.m., there was a sports meet, a bicycle race, and a martial arts performance. (3) It was requested that the Construction Department announce the account of the cocoon collection in the previous season. The Steamship Association held a general meeting of members at its location on Guangdong Road yesterday afternoon. What Was Heard About the Opening of the Shanghai-Xiang Intercity Train on the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway 124

The Shanghai-Xiang double track built by the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway has long been completed. However, due to the fact that various facilities such as signals are still being prepared, it is currently not possible to officially use it as a double track. The railway plans to temporarily use the newly added track from May 1 to test the opening of the Shanghai-Xiang intercity passenger train by steam locomotive, and added stops at Zhongshan Road and Jiangqiao Station. It was reported in the previous newspaper that the intercity train runs 12 times a day in each direction. In Shanghai, the first train departs at 5:10 a.m. After that, the train departs once every one hour and thirty minutes for the next three times. For the fifth and sixth times, the departure time is one hour and twenty-five minutes after the last departure. For the seventh to ninth times, the departure time is one hour and forty minutes after the last departure. For the tenth to twelfth times, the departure time is one hour and thirty minutes after the last departure. Therefore, people coming from Nanxiang can take the train back to Xiang at 10:00 p.m. In Nanxiang, the first train departs at 5:50 a.m. and the last one at 10:40 p.m. From now on, it is very convenient to travel between Shanghai and Xiang. The monthly ticket price is particularly low, regardless of grade. Except for Jiangqiao and Nanxiang, where the fare is one cent, each other station is only five cents. The fare for the entire distance between Shanghai and Nanxiang is only 25 cents. The ticket sales and boarding and alighting place in Shanghai is at the north end of Zaoqiao. However, passengers are not allowed to carry heavy luggage except for light items carried with them. (If there is heavy luggage, you can take other ordinary trains at Shangbei Main Station). Also, Shanghai-Xiang intercity trains do not issue through tickets. However, round-trip tickets and periodical tickets, i.e., monthly tickets, are all accepted.

Silk Industry Bank Promotes Acceptance Drafts 126

Besides accepting discounting, it can also be used as collateral, facilitating commercial transactions and creating a new chapter.

Since the Shanghai Silk and Satin Trade Association and the Shanghai Silk Industry Bank have vigorously promoted commercial acceptance drafts, all parties have agreed. As for the discounting aspect, it has also been resolved by the Bankers Association of Shanghai, and all banks in the association will handle it without any problems. As for the discounting procedures, in order to unify the banks, a sub-committee has been organized to discuss and formulate various documents. The Central Bank has also promised rediscounting. Various industries, such as electrical machinery silk weaving factories, equipment dyeing and weaving industries, cotton cloth industry, and egg industry, have all agreed to implement it. In terms of promotion, it can be said that it is gradually becoming concrete. It is learned that the Silk Industry Bank, which has been the most vigorous in promoting this type of draft, has accepted many discounting cases in recent days. The discount rate is very low, intending to make it gradually popular through promotion. The bank is also concerned that various industries may not be very clear about the style of acceptance drafts and discounting procedures, so it has printed a whole book of drafts for purchase by all sectors, and also printed "Discounting Guidelines" for free collection. Recently, in view of the needs of commercial transactions, it has newly created commercial deposits, which can entrust the bank to collect commercial acceptance drafts on its behalf. If the bank agrees, it can also be used as collateral. The bank's discounting guidelines and commercial deposit regulations are excerpted and attached below:

Discounting Guidelines

Discounting Guidelines for Commercial Acceptance Drafts: (1) Any merchant or manufacturer who holds an acceptance draft and intends to discount it at this bank should first fill out an application form. (2) If the bank considers it qualified, it will immediately notify the applicant to go through the discounting procedures. (3) The number of days for discounting bills shall not exceed a certain number of days at most. (4) The discount rate and the discount amount shall be negotiated by the applicant and the bank at any time. (5) The discounted bill shall be endorsed by the discounter and transferred to the bank. (6) The stamp duty to be affixed on the discounted bill shall be handled by the discounter. (7) If the bill is not paid upon maturity, the bank may exercise the right of recourse against any one of the drawer, endorser, and guarantor. (8) After the bill is paid upon maturity, the bank will immediately return the bill to the payer.

Deposit Regulations

(1) Any company or firm that opens a business in this city can apply to the bank to open an account with an initial deposit of one hundred yuan. Upon the bank's approval, a check will be issued for withdrawal. (2) The monthly interest rate is three percent. If the daily balance is above 500 yuan, an additional half percent will be given. If the daily balance is above 1,000 yuan, an additional one percent will be given. Compound interest will be calculated monthly and a statement will be sent. (3) If the bank is entrusted to collect commercial acceptance drafts, no handling fee will be charged. If the bank agrees, it can also be used as collateral.

Candy Industry Association Protects Members' Business 127

Products that have passed the sanitation bureau's chemical tests are submitted to the two county governments for review.

The Candy Industry Association reported that many candy factories have reported to the association that it has been reported in recent days that peddlers selling candy in various villages and towns within the borders of the two counties of Chuansha and Baoshan have been using candy containing toxic substances to lure children. Many of those who eat it are poisoned to death. The rumor has spread and everyone is talking about it. The local public security bureau is strictly cracking down on it. The wind is blowing fiercely, and even shops selling candy are searched. Therefore, customers in the area have returned their goods one after another, fearing that the entire candy industry will be hit. The association believes that this matter is of great importance. Yesterday afternoon, it convened a meeting of candy group members to discuss protection measures. More than 20 candy factory representatives attended. As a result of the discussion, it was requested that the county governments of Chuansha and Baoshan order their respective public security bureaus to review the peddlers selling candy when cracking down on them, and also request that they not involve stores. A list of candy factories was attached to the presentation to assist in the investigation. It is learned that most of the candy factories in this city are members of the association, and all products have been sampled and tested by the Municipal Health Bureau and found to be qualified.

Route

The fourth public bus route will start on May 1. Fares

The fare ranges from 5 cents to 23 cents, divided into 10 stops. One stop is 5 cents, two stops are 7 cents, three stops are 9 cents, four stops are 11 cents, five stops are 13 cents, six stops are 15 cents, seven stops are 17 cents, eight stops are 19 cents, nine stops are 20 cents, and ten stops are 23 cents. The calling stations along the way are also calculated by stops (for example, if you get off at a calling station in the middle of Station A and Station B, you must count to Station B. If you get on at a calling station, you must count from Station A).

American Warship Collides with Pig Boat 130

Sun Qiugen Drowns in the Huangpu River, All Pigs on Board Disappear

Wang Asan from Nanhui, along with his friends Cao Lansheng and Tao Langqing, recently collected 62 pigs raised by villagers in the Chenjiaqiao area of Pudong. 41 pigs were under the name of Wang Asan, 13 pigs were under the name of Cao Lansheng, and 8 pigs were under the name of Tao Langqing. They hired Sun Qiugen (26 years old, from Nanhui)'s barge to load them and planned to transport them to Jiangwan Town for delivery. At 4:18 am the day before yesterday (the 27th), Sun Qiugen's pig boat was sailing in the Huangpu River near Gaoqiao. The American warship "Finchi" (transliteration) was sailing into the port. The two ships were close together. Sun Qiugen saw it and wanted to avoid it, but the current was too fast and it was too late. At that time, the sky was not yet bright, and there was a drizzle and heavy fog. The warship was sailing extremely fast. In an instant, a tragedy occurred. The bow of the warship crashed into the stern of Sun Qiugen's boat. With a loud bang, Sun's boat was immediately shattered and capsized. Everyone on board fell into the water. Except for Wang Asan, Cao Lansheng, Tao Langqing, etc., who were rescued and survived, Sun Qiugen had already joined the wave god. All 62 pigs on board fell into the Huangpu River and disappeared. Afterwards, Wang Asan and others reported to the water patrol police station, requesting to salvage Sun Qiugen's body and demanding compensation for the damage from the warship. Yesterday morning, the salvage bureau's patrol boat salvaged Sun Qiugen's body in the Huangpu River south of Gaoqiao and brought it to Nantou Wharf for examination. A detective named Liang Shenqing was dispatched by the police chief to summon the deceased's wife, Sun Gu, and Wang Asan, Cao Lansheng, etc., to prepare a letter to be transferred to the local court. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Dian Binzhang conducted an interrogation and then led investigator Xuan Zhiming to the scene. After examining Sun Qiugen's body, it was confirmed that he had drowned. An order was issued for the family to collect the body and await further investigation.

Special Court Investigates Jailbreak Case 131

More Internal and External Guards Suspected, Jailbreak Inmate Demonstrates Jailbreak Truth

Murderer Chen Jinlan escaped from the Special Second District Court detention center on the morning of December 27 last year. The warden immediately transferred the guards of the upper and lower three shifts to the prosecutor's office. As a result of the investigation, it was found that the internal guard of the three to seven shifts, Fang Yuqi, and the external guard, Zhou Wenjin, were suspected of facilitating the escape. They were prosecuted and sentenced to imprisonment. The police station arrested Chen and sent him to the court. The prosecutor interrogated him and filed a public prosecution. The Wang prosecutor opened a court hearing to investigate the situation the day before yesterday, which has been reported in the newspaper. It is learned that in order to clarify the detailed process of Chen's escape, the Wang prosecutor dispatched police officers to the police station at 3 pm yesterday to transfer Chen to the case and bring him to the detention center. A small section of fine lead wire was given to Chen to make a key on the spot and demonstrate the process of unlocking and escaping. Then, a court hearing was opened to interrogate Chen and Yang and Yan for a long time. An order was issued to return them to the detention center to await further investigation.

Lu Shaotang Flees, Huafeng Case Adjourned 132

Xu Guannan is not a Huafeng shareholder and requests not to be liable for debt.

Lu Shaotang and others jointly opened the Huafeng Xingji Flour Company in 1929. In recent years, the business has declined, losses have accumulated, and it has been unable to maintain it, so it has closed down. The debts owed, just to the Qianye (money shops), have reached more than 277,200 yuan. The Da De and other 27 Qian Zhuang (money shops) have jointly filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court against the shareholders of the factory, Lu Shaotang, Ye Shantao, Xu Guannan, etc. It has been reported in the previous newspapers. It is learned that after Xu Guannan received the court summons, he hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to submit a statement stating that he had withdrawn his shares and should no longer be liable for debt. According to his statement, when the factory was organized, Lu Shaotang attached 50% of the shares, and he and Ye Shantao each attached 25% of the shares. Later, because he was getting older and weaker, he did not intend to partner, and formally withdrew his shares in June 1931. At that time, Hua Fu was still self-sufficient, so more than 34,560 taels of capital silver were returned when he withdrew his shares. The money pursued by the original plaintiffs are all debts after he withdrew his shares, so there is no need to be jointly responsible. It is requested that the part of the lawsuit against him be dismissed. The case was heard again by Judge Peng the day before yesterday, but Lu Shaotang, who is actually responsible for Huafeng, has recently fled due to other cases, so it is still impossible to summon him. The court then ordered the hearing to be adjourned.

Public Works Bureau Discusses the Organization of the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association 135

In August last year, the Public Works Bureau drafted a plan for the organization of the rickshaw pullers' mutual aid association, which could be reconsidered after eight months. Recently, at the request of the rickshaw owners' association, a meeting was convened at the Public Works Bureau yesterday morning (the 29th). Five people, including Mr. Yin Zhiling, attended on behalf of the rickshaw owners. The Public Works Bureau was chaired by Director-General Faithunton. Attendees included the deputy director and three members of the rickshaw committee. The rickshaw owners' side made a statement regarding the monthly collection of 1.5 yuan for the mutual aid association fee. The chairman stated that this issue was not on the agenda for discussion, as the Public Works Bureau's established policy was that rickshaw owners must cooperate with the mutual aid association in order to be granted a rickshaw license. The organization issue was then discussed. The rickshaw owners' representatives proposed sending people to join the fund committee. The chairman of the rickshaw committee replied that this was not appropriate, as the fund committee members must be very enthusiastic about seeking welfare for the rickshaw pullers. If the rickshaw owners' association joins, it will inevitably cause obstacles. Moreover, the rickshaw owners already have two representatives in the board of directors. If the fund committee members do not act in accordance with the board of directors' policy, the board of directors can appeal to the Public Works Bureau. The rickshaw owners' representatives then proposed adjourning the meeting in order to discuss it with the executive committee of the association. The chairman of the rickshaw committee then asked whether the association was willing to continue to collect the rickshaw licenses for the next month according to the current method (that is, the 1.5 yuan fee will still be collected). The association representatives said that if there is no other agreement within the day, the rickshaw owners will continue to handle it as before in May. The meeting was then adjourned and will be continued after the rickshaw owners' side has reached a decision.

The invitation reads: "The National Government has issued an order to award the Caiyu Medal to Mr. Du Yuesheng, Mr. Zhang Xiaolin, Mr. Huang Jinrong, Mr. Han Yungen, Mr. Xu Maotang, and Mr. Wu Ruiyuan for their enthusiastic disaster relief or fundraising, and for donating more than 200,000 yuan in national currency or more than 50,000 yuan in disaster relief funds, which were forwarded by the Xinwei Relief Association to the National Government through the Executive Yuan. The award ceremony will be held at the Huangjia Garden in Caohejing at 1 pm on May 1. Lunch will be prepared. Respectfully invite your presence. Sincerely, Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Central Disaster Relief Committee."

Record of the Shangchuan Company Shareholders' General Meeting 140

It was decided to extend the road line to Nanhui and add 600,000 preferred shares.

Shangchuan Transportation Company has been operating the long-distance tramcar business from Shanghai to Chuansha. The business has been developing well and the results have been remarkable in recent years. On the 28th of this month, the 11th Shareholders' General Meeting was held at the company's office in Qingning Temple to discuss important matters such as extending the Nanchuan Road line and increasing capital. By 1 pm, a total of 230 shareholders were present, with more than 11,000 shares, and the number of shareholders and shares both exceeded half. The meeting was convened immediately, and Chairman Qu Shaoyi was elected as the chairman. First, Manager Gu Baowei reported on the progress and business conditions of the past year, stating that the Nanchuan Road line has been urged by local people. After the board of directors was entrusted with the decision made at last year's shareholders' general meeting, the Nanchuan and Chuanqin road line contracts were signed with the Nanhui and Chuansha county governments respectively in May last year, and they were submitted to the provincial authorities for approval. The Chuanqin line, from Sizao Port outside the North Gate of Chuansha to the Nanhui border of Xiaoyingfang, has been paved and opened to traffic. The Nanchuan line has also been surveyed and mapped, and construction will begin soon. The operating income for the past year was 227,000 yuan. After deducting expenses and setting aside public reserves and depreciation, the net profit was more than 44,000 yuan. Next, Supervisor Lu Wenmei reported on the accounting. The shareholders approved it on the spot, and then discussed the proposals. 1. The dividend distribution proposal was decided to be distributed at the official rate of 1%, with more than 4,000 yuan remaining to be added to the public reserves. 2. The company's capital is 400,000 yuan. After experts estimated that the current fixed assets are worth more than 630,000 yuan, the original value of the company's assets since its establishment has been more than 900,000 yuan. After depreciation and reserves and preparation funds, the net profit is more than 100,000 yuan. Now, because of the extension of the road line, it is necessary to add capital. How should this surplus be handled? It was decided to distribute 100,000 yuan to the shareholders as new shares, and the directors and supervisors stated that in addition to the dividend for this year to ordinary shareholders, all directors and supervisors would use the dividends they should receive as new shares. 3. The extension of the Nanchuan Road line requires amending the articles of association and increasing capital. First, the chairman explained that extending the road line to Nanhui would cost more than 600,000 yuan. After detailed discussions among the shareholders, it was decided to continue to solicit 30,000 preferred shares, totaling 600,000 yuan. The preferred shares have the benefit of preferential distribution of official interest and preferential repayment of capital within six years. In addition to the previous surplus of 100,000 yuan, which is distributed to old shareholders according to the original share amount, there are still 25,000 shares. According to the regulations, old shareholders have the right to subscribe for shares first. However, there are many requests from all parties to subscribe for shares. For the sake of universality, 15,000 shares are specially made available for subscription by people other than old shareholders and in the area where the road line is extended. Next, supervisors were elected. As a result, Wei Yuping, Lu Wenmei, and Cai Guocai were elected with the most votes. The meeting ended at 6 pm. It is heard that the company's approach to doing things has always been steady and pragmatic, striving for truth from facts everywhere and striving to save on expenses. Therefore, although the recent recession has spread across the country, the company's business has been increasing year by year, making it rare for shareholders to still have 1% of the official interest. The experts who were hired to estimate the fixed assets of the accounting company were Mr. Li Qianruo, the dean of the School of Engineering of Jiaotong University, Mr. Wang Shengsan, the vice president of the Chinese Society of Civil Engineers and the director of the Investigation Section of the Four Banks Savings Association, and Mr. Shi Zhiren, the deputy director of the Machinery Department of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways. They are all well-known engineering and mechanical experts. After on-site detailed estimation, they issued a certificate and were responsible for proving it. The company currently extends to Xiaoyingfang in Chuansha, which is only more than 40 li long. If it is extended to Datuan in Nanhui, it will increase by more than 50 li, so that people from Nanhui can reach Shanghai in less than four hours. Not only will it facilitate local transportation, but it can also be predicted that the business will be even more developed.

Thugs Make Strong Threats and Intimidate Securities Firm Owner: 144

The Demand Reduced from 20,000 to 15,000 Yuan. Detective Intervenes to Negotiate and Arrest a Thug.

Wei Chao Geng, a Ningbo native residing at No. 12 Shangwen Lane, Weihaiwei Road, operates the Dayuan Securities Firm at No. 11 Meiren Lane, Hankou Road. Since March 31st of this year, Wei and his Ningbo hometown have received five threatening letters from a gang identifying themselves as the "Guoye Zongshe," alleging that Wei inherited hundreds of thousands of yuan from his father's estate and requesting a contribution of 20,000 yuan to their operating expenses. The letters used strong and intimidating language. Wei ignored the letters. However, in the past two days, Wei's relative, He Wenhua (accountant at the Dazhongyang Shoes Factory, No. 241 Ningguo Road), also received two threatening letters from the same organization, asking him to forward them. The amount requested had been reduced from 20,000 to 15,000 yuan, and they arranged to meet at the roof garden entrance of the Sincere Company between 8:00 and 9:00 PM the night before. The person was instructed to hold a newspaper in one hand and carry a Madunhe hatbox in the other as a sign. Someone would approach them for negotiations, but they were strictly forbidden from bringing many followers. Failure to comply would result in "appropriate measures." Wei sent He Wenhua as his representative and reported the matter to the Chengdu Road Police Station at 6:30 AM the previous morning. Detective Xie Guisheng, Western Detective Harvard, and others were dispatched to keep watch. He Wenhua followed the instructions in the letter and arrived at the Sincere Company's main entrance, carrying a newspaper and hatbox. Soon after, Zhu Zhongwu, a Shaoxing native, approached He and confirmed that he was Wei's representative. They went up to the roof garden to have tea and discuss the matter. He stated that Wei did not have such a large sum of money and could only borrow ten or twenty yuan, or perhaps pay according to his means, but the difference in amount was too great to negotiate. He then removed his hat as prearranged, and the Chinese and Western detectives rushed in and arrested Zhu, taking him to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police station's lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, charged him under Article 370 of the Criminal Code and stated that the case required further investigation of accomplices and verification of handwriting, requesting a postponement. Judge Yang Zhaoqi reviewed the confession and ordered Zhu to be remanded in custody, with the hearing postponed to next Wednesday.

French Police in Concession Arbitrarily Interfere with Store's Gong and Drum Music; Second Special District Fourth Branch Sends Letter to French Police Requesting Rectification 145

The Fourth District Branch of the Shanghai Second Special District Citizens' Union, located near the Nanyang Bridge in the French Concession, was holding a 15th-anniversary celebration for its member Gao Maoshengtang Chinese Medicine Store at Nos. 154 and 156 Rue Lafayette. A number of gong and drum players were hired to perform at the store to mark the occasion. Unexpectedly, at 9:00 AM on the 27th of this month, French Police Officer No. 96 and Chinese Police Officer No. 177 arrived to stop the performance and recorded the store's address to impose an arbitrary fine, leading the union to request intervention. After learning the details, the union sent a letter to the French Superintendent yesterday requesting a rectification. The original letter is transcribed below: To the esteemed Superintendent: According to a letter from Gao Maoshengtang Chinese Medicine Store, a member of this union located at Nos. 154 and 156 Rue Lafayette, the store is currently holding its 15th-anniversary celebration, offering special deals for one month, and has hired a number of gong and drum players to perform at the store to mark the occasion. Unexpectedly, at 9:00 AM on the 27th of this month, while the performers were playing at the store, French Police Officer No. 96 and Chinese Police Officer No. 177 arrived to stop the performance and asked if they had obtained a permit. The store immediately stated that they had never obtained a permit for anniversary celebrations and that there was no reason to pay a permit fee for performing inside the store. Despite their explanation, the Western police officer was unreasonable and ordered the performance to stop, also recording the store's address to impose a fine. The store's special anniversary sale does not violate any police regulations, and the Western police officer abused his authority by unreasonably obstructing business, making it difficult for merchants to operate. They immediately reported the matter to the responsible police station, which replied that a fine of two yuan was to be paid. However, they did not allow the store to explain the situation. It is clear that the police officer unreasonably interfered with the gong and drum music and is now falsely claiming it was a street obstruction, arbitrarily imposing a fine. Such unreasonable punishment is unacceptable, and we hereby request that your esteemed office intervene based on reason to ensure business is conducted peacefully. According to this, we have found that police officers have recently been creating unnecessary trouble by arbitrarily fining shops when recording their addresses. This has been happening daily, and this union has received reports from members repeatedly. In this case, the Western police officer's unreasonable harassment of merchants is particularly obvious. We respectfully request that your esteemed Superintendent investigate and correct this matter promptly.

Retired Military Officer Sued by Maid: 146

Accused of Abandonment after Seduction and Stealing the Child; Lawsuit Seeks Alimony and Education Expenses

Deng Jianhao, a Hubei native and former military officer residing in a Western-style house at No. 589 Rue du Père Robert in the French Concession, had several concubines during his tenure as a division commander before 1930. Having already one wife and three concubines, he spent 5,000 yuan to take Mei Ying, a Haiment woman, as his fourth concubine, introduced by his servant Liu Xiangtai, who was from Haimen. Liu also arranged for his fellow villager, Cheng Di, whom he had previously purchased and adopted as a goddaughter, to serve as Mei Ying's dowry maid. In 1930, Deng was ordered to lead his troops to Jiangxi to suppress bandits, but unfortunately, he failed and was dismissed by his superiors, placed under supervision, and then sent to the Lu Army Prison in Nanjing to await investigation. At that time, Mei Ying also lived in Nanjing and often had Cheng Di visit the prison to deliver clothes and other items.

He Bribed Guards and Forcibly Defiled Her.

However, Deng saw that Cheng Di was young and beautiful, and he harbored improper thoughts. He bribed the prison guards and, when Cheng Di came to visit the prison, he forcibly defiled her in the reception room. Afterward, he promised her that after his release, he would take her as a concubine and told her to wait patiently. Soon after, Deng was released with the help of an important figure. However, after Deng was released, he broke his promise to Cheng Di. Cheng Di felt wronged and recently hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the criminal court of the Second Special District Court, accusing Deng Jianhao of abduction and rape, malicious abandonment, and Liu Xiangtai of abduction.

Interfering with a Family, and restricting her freedom.

Interfering with a family, interfering with freedom, and enslavement. She also filed a civil suit seeking alimony, the return of her child, and educational expenses, totaling 41,280 yuan. Her statement of claim states that the plaintiff lost her mother at a young age and was orphaned. She met Liu Xiangtai, the second defendant, a fellow villager, who tricked her into becoming his adopted daughter. In 1929, Liu Xiangtai sold another woman named Mei Ying to Deng Jianhao, the first defendant, as his fourth concubine for 5,000 yuan, and ordered the plaintiff to go with her as a maid. In 1930, the first defendant was accused of greed and illegal activities while suppressing bandits in Jiangxi and was detained in the Nanjing Lu Army Prison, in a solitary cell. The plaintiff, on Mei Ying's orders, often went to deliver items. Unexpectedly, the first defendant dared to

Bribe the Guards

to rape a girl under the age of sixteen and forbid her from speaking out. After his release, he made sweet promises, saying he would take her as a concubine in the future, while secretly monitoring her and preventing her from going out. The plaintiff, under his control, had no choice but to submit to his abuse. In December 1933, the plaintiff became pregnant. In May of the following year, she was heavily pregnant. At that time, the first defendant and his fourth concubine, Mei Ying, agreed that it was inconvenient to give birth at home and insisted that she return to her hometown of Haimen to await delivery, promising to come and pick her up after the birth. On October 16th of the following year, she

Gave Birth to a Son

At Chenshi, on the 26th, Deng's fourth concubine, Mei Ying, returned to Haimen and carried the child away. Because the child was not yet a month old, she was not allowed to take him. Later, Deng personally

Sent a Letter to Mei Ying

which contained the words, "Do as I say, no matter what, first bring the child back." The original letter is still in existence. On November 19th of the same year, Deng sent someone to Haimen again to forcibly take the child away, disregarding the plaintiff's life or death. Although she repeatedly sent letters requesting living expenses, the first defendant initially ignored them and then returned the original letters. Since then, there has been no news and no communication. The plaintiff claims that the first defendant was greedy and unlawful in office, and promiscuous in private. He raped a minor virgin and forcibly took away the child. Not only is the infant child separated from his mother, endangering his life, but his abandonment after seduction is

Inhumane and Cruel

beyond measure. His actions violate Article 240, Paragraph 1, and Article 309, Paragraph 1, of the Criminal Code, and the second defendant violates Article 257, Paragraph 1, and Article 313, Paragraph 1, of the same code. She is therefore filing a self-accusation and also a civil suit, requesting that the first defendant pay the plaintiff alimony of 50 yuan per month from the age of 21 to 60, totaling 24,000 yuan, and return the child, as well as pay for the child's educational expenses, averaging 60 yuan per month, up to 1935, totaling 17,280 yuan, for a total of 41,280 yuan, etc. When the court dispatched bailiffs to serve the summons at the defendant's residence, the family replied that the defendant

Had Gone to Hankou

and no one accepted the summons. Therefore, at the court hearing on the 9th of this month, the defendants failed to appear. The plaintiff's lawyer requested a warrant to be issued, which the plaintiff would serve. The court approved the request and scheduled a new hearing. Judge Zhang Chaozuo issued a summons and dispatched bailiffs to serve the summons at the defendant's address, but the defendant had moved away with his entire family and no one accepted the summons. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhang held a hearing, but both defendants

Still Absent,

Only the plaintiff and her lawyer appeared in court. After the court inquired about the circumstances of the summons, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that the defendant was still in Shanghai, residing on Beile Road, and requested that an arrest warrant be issued under Article 50 of the Criminal Procedure Law, as the defendant was at risk of fleeing. The court said that an arrest warrant is not a search warrant, and it's not okay to go to people's homes to search. Now that the defendant has failed to appear twice, the court can only suspend the trial proceedings. In the future, there will be a ruling served, and after the plaintiff receives the ruling, she will know where the defendant is. She can then take the ruling to report to the police station and have them arrest him, or notify the court to bring him in for trial. There's no need to issue an arrest warrant to be served. After the argument, the court declared adjournment.

Changye Real Estate Company Sues Lu Xihou for Repayment of Mortgage Loan 149

Verdict to be Announced on May 6th

All real estate of Guomin Hotel Nos. 26 and 28 at the intersection of Tianzhutang Street and Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession belongs to Lu Xihou, the chairman of the bankrupt China Xingye Bank. Lu mortgaged this real estate to the British-owned Changye Real Estate Company for 250,000 taels of silver, equivalent to 349,650.35 yuan, with interest calculated at 8% per month. After the collapse of China Xingye Bank last year, the First Special District Court entrusted the Second Special District Court to attach this real estate. Now, the creditor Changye Real Estate Company, managed by a Westerner named Moore (transliteration), hired lawyer Chen Zhongyin to file a lawsuit in the Second Special District Court against Lu, seeking repayment of the loan and interest from last October until the end of the execution. The court accepted the case and yesterday morning, Judge Ma Yishu held a hearing in the Seventh Civil Court. Both plaintiffs and defendants, each accompanied by their lawyers, appeared in court. The plaintiff first stated the facts of the lawsuit and the object of the judgment. Then, the defendant Lu Xihou was questioned, and he admitted the mortgage and said he would find a way to repay it to redeem the property. He said that the litigation costs were huge and he could not afford them, requesting that the plaintiff be ordered to assume them. As for the interest, he would pay it up to December 18th of last year, but after that, due to the collapse of China Xingye Bank, he was placed under court custody and stopped paying interest. After the arguments of both lawyers, the court declared the hearing concluded and scheduled the verdict to be announced on May 6th.

All iron and copper ware, such as automobiles, chartered cars, bicycles, copper signs, copper railings, electric fans, electric stoves, household appliances, and all hospital equipment, will last for a long time and will not change color, not only beautiful, but also save the daily trouble of oiling, etc. For the sake of promoting business, the plating fee is even lower, and goods are picked up within a limited number of days, and there will be no breach of contract. Call 37104 to notify the factory and they will send someone to discuss the matter.

Special Announcement

Bank of Communications Business Report (4) 167

I. A Glimmer of Economic Improvement in China

As previously mentioned, China's economy is suffering from the pressure of foreign inflation and the impact of controlled economies, resulting in massive trade deficits and silver outflows, creating a declining economic picture. However, in the past year, public and private economic enterprises have shown signs of improvement in their efforts to cope with this environment through defense and adjustment, as well as internal development. A few key points are outlined below:

(1) Matters Related to Finance and Construction: (A) Public bonds and treasury bills that have been consolidated are being repaid on schedule with both principal and interest. Bonds issued this year, including foreign currency bonds and those issued by various provinces, total approximately 220 million yuan. Local bonds are mainly focused on construction and disaster relief. (B) National taxes have been consolidated, and customs and salt taxes have been revised. Over 3,600 kinds of arbitrary taxes and levies have been abolished. (C) Important construction projects, such as the diversion of the Huai River, the control of the Yellow River, the diversion of the Wei River, the port development of Pukou, and the Qiantang River Bridge, have either been completed or are under construction. Factories for manufacturing machine alcohol, ammonium sulfate, etc., are being established one after another. Steel and newspaper factories are also in the planning stages. These efforts are aimed at strengthening the foundations of both public and private economies.

(2) Matters Related to Currency and Exchange Rates: (A) Currency Consolidation: The Ministry of Finance has issued a ban on private currencies and banknotes. (B) Exchange Rate Management: Measures include the implementation of silver export duties and equalization taxes, as well as the successive establishment of the Exchange Stabilization Fund and the Currency System Committee. In addition, speculative bidding has been prohibited, and the Central Bank is now responsible for setting the daily exchange rate. Although the effects are not yet significant, the unification of currency and the management of exchange rates have at least begun.

(3) Matters Related to Transportation: (A) Railway Projects: Major projects include the extension of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway to Nanchang, the extension of the Longhai Railway to Xi'an, the connection of the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway, the construction of the Huainan Railway to Hefei, and the construction of the Jingzhao section of the Beijing-Wuhu Railway. These projects are actively underway and will connect urban and inland areas, facilitating the transportation of goods. (B) Highway Projects: The Seven-Province Interconnection Highway, with a total length of over 22,000 kilometers, has 3,290 kilometers already open to traffic (according to the Economic Commission Highway Administration's December report). The highways in the three northwestern provinces, Gansu and Qinghai, total over 10,000 li. In Ningxia, highways extend south to Guyuan and north to Linhe, and are either completed or under construction. In addition, provinces such as Hebei and Fujian are building their own highways, which, according to surveys, total over 30,000 kilometers, further facilitating inland transportation and the marketing of local products. (Improvements in telephone services are omitted here for brevity.) (C) Improved Transportation Services: Joint freight transport on railways such as the Beijing-Shanghai, Pingpu, and Longhai lines has been implemented, and responsible transportation is also in effect. The sale of local products through railway business offices provides a convenient shortcut for the production and marketing of local goods, facilitating the transportation of goods.

(4) Matters Related to Production and Marketing: (A) In terms of domestic production, Guangdong's light and heavy industries have developed considerably. Imports of light industrial products such as cotton cloth and paper have decreased, indicating a potential resurgence of these domestic goods. (B) Product and marketing controls: Silk cocoons and cotton yarn are subject to the organization of control committees. (C) Cooperative enterprises: According to a survey by the Central Agricultural Experiment Station, there are a total of 14,649 cooperatives nationwide. Credit cooperatives account for over 76%, while those managing production and marketing account for 8.9%. As a result, although wharves may decline and middlemen may lose their profits, these efforts are significantly effective in improving the production and marketing of domestic goods.

(5) Matters Related to Financial Services: (A) The Savings Bank Law has been promulgated, and regulations on savings reserves have been established. (B) Branches of various banks are being established and expanded, moving into the interior and providing agricultural loans, gradually channeling funds back into rural areas. (C) Urban money shops are becoming more like banks, and inland banks are establishing offices in nearby villages and towns, a trend some call the "bank-ification" of money shops. (D) In terms of cooperation among banks, loans to the government for construction and disaster relief total nearly 130 million yuan for the year. In terms of cooperation and mutual assistance among peers, in addition to joint reserves and bill exchanges, banks are collaborating on loans or jointly running secondary businesses, adhering to the principle of unified action to avoid competition. This is an improvement in financial services.

In addition, the victories in bandit suppression, the stability of the situation in Shaanxi and Henan, and the good harvests in Jiangbei, Hebei, and the Northwest are fortunate. The upward trend in bond prices, with no drastic fluctuations throughout the year, also shows a gradual stabilization of public sentiment. Some say that improvements in the management of finance, the organization of cooperative industries, etc., are now beginning to show results. The gradual implementation of the mortgage system and the closer proximity of production to transportation and consumption may also be signs of gradual improvement in the economy.

As described above, although these are just the starting points of improvement efforts, they are indeed a glimmer of hope for the economy. Just like a chronically ill person who receives proper care, a positive turnaround can be expected. Banks, with their position of maintaining and assisting, should do their best to fulfill their responsibilities, and our bank, with its mission to develop industry, must work hard to achieve this. The work of the past year has shown considerable results. Fortunately, banks are now shifting from individual competition to a united front, cooperating to serve society. This is another positive development among peers, which can be viewed with optimism. (To be continued)

Education News

Educational Interpretation: Measures for Students from the Puppet Manchukuo to Study 168

The Ministry of Education received a request from Shanghai Private Law School regarding Luo Songqiu, a graduate of a senior high school established in the puppet state of Manchukuo, who sought admission. The school inquired whether the qualifications of such students were recognized and whether their graduation certificates were valid, as no explicit regulations had been issued by the ministry. The ministry instructed the school to inform the student that graduation certificates issued by puppet organizations could not be recognized as valid. However, if the student wished to study in the mainland, they could apply to the Northeast Youth Education Relief Agency for screening and testing in accordance with the "Provisional Measures for Northeast Students Entering and Transferring to Schools." According to Article 1 of the measures, students from areas relatively distant from the peace could be examined by the local educational administrative authority entrusted by the agency for the purpose of providing relief.

Guangdong Province Restricts the Establishment of Private Middle Schools and Improves Existing Ones 169

The Guangdong Provincial Department of Education has formulated measures to restrict the establishment of private middle schools and promote improvements, which have been approved by the provincial government. The minimum standards for opening private middle schools are as follows:

(A) Minimum Standards for Opening Private Junior High Schools in the Provincial Capital: "School Land and Buildings" should include an auditorium, office, classrooms (three rooms), laboratory, library, and sports field. "Equipment" should include instruments worth 2,500 yuan, specimens and models worth 1,500 yuan, books worth 2,000 yuan, and school and teaching supplies worth 2,000 yuan. "Operating Expenses" should include rental income from assets or funds, plus other fixed income, reaching 1,185 yuan per month. Those running only one class may reduce this by one-half, and those running two classes may reduce it by one-third. (B) Minimum Standards for Adding Senior High Schools to Private Junior High Schools in the Provincial Capital: "School Land and Buildings" should include an auditorium, office, classrooms (six rooms), physics, chemistry, and biology laboratories, library, and sports field. "Equipment" should include instruments worth 4,000 yuan, specimens and models worth 2,500 yuan, books worth 3,000 yuan, and school and teaching supplies worth 3,000 yuan. "Operating Expenses" should include rental income from assets or funds, plus other fixed income, reaching 2,603 yuan per month. Those adding only one class may reduce this by 800 yuan, and those adding two classes may reduce it by 400 yuan. (C) Minimum Standards for Opening Private Junior High Schools in Various Counties and Cities: "School Land and Buildings" should include an auditorium, office, classrooms (three rooms), science laboratory, library, and sports field. "Equipment" should include instruments worth 1,500 yuan, specimens and models worth 1,000 yuan, books worth 1,000 yuan, and school and teaching supplies worth 1,500 yuan. "Operating Expenses" should include assets or funds, plus other fixed income, reaching 900 yuan per month. Those running only one class may reduce this by one-half, and those running two classes may reduce it by one-third. (D) Minimum Standards for Adding Senior High Schools to Private Junior High Schools in Various Counties and Cities: "School Land and Buildings" should include an auditorium, office, classrooms (six rooms), physics, chemistry, and biology laboratories, library, and sports field. "Equipment" should include physical and chemical instruments worth 3,000 yuan, natural history specimens and models worth 2,000 yuan, books worth 2,500 yuan, and school and teaching supplies worth 2,500 yuan. "Operating Expenses" should include rental income from assets or funds, plus other fixed income, reaching 2,000 yuan per month. Those adding only one class may reduce this by 800 yuan, and those adding two classes may reduce it by 400 yuan. (Supplementary Provisions) All schools that have been approved to open or register but fail to meet the opening standards must supplement them in stages within three semesters, starting from this semester. Those who fail to supplement within the time limit in the first stage will be warned. Those who fail to supplement within the time limit in the second stage will be stopped from recruiting new students. Those who still fail to meet the standards at the end of the 24th year will have their registration or opening approval revoked.

Students at Guangdong's Zhongda High School Oppose the Joint Examination, Leading to a Serious Strike 170

Principal Zou Lu Held a School Board Meeting Yesterday and Expelled the Leading Students. The Students' Attitude is Firm, and the Education Department Decided to Comply with the Law.

(Guangzhou News) More than 300 students in the 24th grade of the Guangdong National Sun Yat-sen University High School have been on strike since the 27th due to their opposition to participating in the Education Department's high school graduation joint examination. The school and the Education Department have taken a very firm stance. The school held a school board meeting yesterday (29th) and planned to expel the leading troublemaking students and limit all students to resume classes. The strike situation may worsen. The details are as follows:

High School Organization

The high school affiliated with Sun Yat-sen University was originally reorganized from the university's preparatory course. In the 19th year, the preparatory course was discontinued and second-year high school students were recruited. In the autumn of the 20th year, all grades of the high school affiliated with the university were merged and co-organized, and first-year students were recruited, thus establishing a high school department with a four-year history. The high school department's school system adopts the academic year system, dividing the general curriculum into two groups, A and B. Students who wish to study liberal arts in the future take the Group A course, and those who wish to study science, engineering, medicine, or agriculture take the Group B course. In order to emphasize the cultivation of talents in Group B, the ratio of Group A to Group B in the recruitment of new students in the 22nd year was 1:6, and in the 23rd year, it was 1:2. Over the years, the school has not participated in the government's past joint examinations because its curriculum and nature are different from other high schools, and most of its students go on to study at the university.

Cause of the Strike

Recently, in order to unify the high school student graduation joint examination, the Ministry of Education issued a notice to the Education Departments of various provinces and national universities that all national, provincial, and municipal high schools or affiliated high schools must participate in the graduation joint examination organized by the highest education administrative agency in the province to show uniformity. The Guangdong Education Department, upon receiving the order, immediately forwarded it to Sun Yat-sen University for reference and requested that the list of high school students for the first semester of this year be sent to the department for numbering. The school authorities decided to participate in the joint examination in June in order to comply with government orders and to show the students' abilities, as the Sun Yat-sen University High School had been criticized by the outside world for its low student level for not participating in the joint examination in previous years.

Student Opposition

After learning about this, the students of Sun Yat-sen University High School held a temporary meeting on the 10th and agreed that since the high school curriculum was different from other schools and they had never participated in the joint examination in the past, they would never participate in this action. At the same time, a method was proposed: if they did not participate in the graduation joint examination, they could at most not enter other universities, but they should be allowed to enter the university department of this school. They asked the principal to accept this opinion. When Principal Zou Lu refused, all 300 students issued a declaration and went on strike on the 27th.

Principal's Attitude

After receiving the students' request, Principal Zou Lu immediately stated that he could not accept it because the graduation joint examination was a national education matter, a matter outside the school, not within the school. However, the joint examination was scheduled for June, which was imminent. The school had no choice but to obey the government's order to hold it. When the Education Department held the high school student joint examination, whether the students participated or not was up to them. He would not care. When the students decided to strike, Zou Lu reported everything to the Southwest Political Affairs Committee and the School Board and scheduled a School Board meeting for the 29th to discuss concrete measures to deal with the situation. As for the Education Department, it stated that it would only follow the government's orders and let the students participate or not participate, and it would not care.

Science Exhibition at Soochow University 172

The science department of Soochow University in Suzhou has complete equipment and has long been famous in the Southeast. In order to meet the needs of the times, Dr. Yang Yongqing, the president of the school, held a science exhibition two years ago, which won a lot of praise. The school held its second exhibition on the 25th, 26th, and 27th of this month, and a brief description is recorded as follows. The popularized science lectures and exhibition were held in the Science Museum and were divided into three parts: physics, chemistry, and biology. The route for visitors and the arrangement of instruments and specimens all complied with the scientific procedure. The heads of each department, such as Dean Pan Shenming of the Chemistry Department, Dr. Li Qingxian of the Physics Department, and Dr. Zhang Hecen of the Biology Department, together with senior students of all levels, were assigned to each department to conduct various experiments and lectures. All visitors who had questions were given repeated instructions until they understood.

Highlights of the Content

(1) Physics Department: Divided into eight rooms, all subjects such as acoustics, optics, mechanics, heat, and electricity were classified and detailed explanations and diagrams were attached. The teachers and students also gave enthusiastic explanations and experiments to make it clear to the visitors. Among them, the electrocardiograph, the huge astronomical telescope, the large vacuum tube for sending international telegrams, and the annual red lights in each room were especially eye-opening for the viewers. According to a receptionist, the school tried its best to purchase domestic products for all instruments and electrical materials, and it was said that the quality of domestic products was not only far superior to that of the eastern neighbors, but also inferior to that of Europe and the United States. (2) The Biology Department had even more categories, such as the animal and plant group, the embryonic inheritance group, the human anatomy group, the animal and plant preparation group, and the economic animal and plant group. The economic animal and plant group was especially interesting. The silkworm paper, oil fruits, and microorganisms for making soy sauce, as well as pathogenic bacteria related to human clothing, food, housing, etc., were all listed in their original form. Professor Liu Chengjian of the school collected more than 100 species of fish, reptiles, and amphibians in Wuxian County, which was especially interesting. Other things such as the evolution of various microscopes and human mechanical diagrams can all give people a general scientific knowledge. The school's attached biological materials office is divided into three parts: skeleton specimens, device specimens, and glass slide specimens. It supplies 50,000 to 60,000 pieces to domestic universities and middle schools every year. In recent years, Western schools have also purchased from the office several times a month. This is not only a meaningful contribution, but also a significant way to prevent leakage. (3) The Chemistry Department is divided into six departments, including physiological industry, organic and inorganic. The food nutrition specimens in the physiology department and the mechanical specimens of vitamin components are especially valuable to the public. Industrial chemistry, such as papermaking, pigments, soaps, distilled water, and gas, all have their manufacturing procedures and chemical steps analyzed in detail. The distilled water item is supplied to all hospitals in Suzhou and has received good reviews. Other things such as gas masks can also give viewers military common sense. The structure of this mask uses the absorption of charcoal. Because charcoal has the property of absorbing odors, toxic gas enters the nostrils through the charcoal tube, which filters and stores the gas, which is harmless to life. In addition, various special phenomena and anomalies in science are too many to describe in detail.

Enthusiasm of the Visitors: The exhibition period was three days. In the first two days, the number of visitors was no less than six or seven thousand. The school also held a calligraphy and painting and flower show at the same time. Although the visitors browsed separately, they were still shoulder to shoulder and overcrowded. The school organized all men and women in the city. All secondary schools suspended classes to visit. There were also people from other cities, such as people from military, commercial, industrial, agricultural, and other sectors, as well as parents of students from the school. From this, it can be seen that the interest of Chinese people in science has gradually increased.

The Graduate Joint Examination Group of the Middle School Normal Education Research Association Continued Its Meeting Yesterday 173

A Detailed Discussion on the Issues of the Graduation Joint Examination System. The Training and Military Group Meeting Will Continue This Afternoon.

The Graduate Joint Examination Group of the Middle School Normal Education Research Association of this city held its second research meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday. The Training and Military Group meeting will continue at Lakeside Club at 2:00 PM this afternoon. The details are recorded as follows:

Graduate Joint Examination Group

Present were Chen Jicheng, Shen Tilan, Feng Yixian, Wu Youxiao, Tao Guangchuan, Tang Naikang, Xu Renhan, Yang Daohong, Wang Zhongming, Jin Yuezhang, Qian Fugong of the Education Bureau, and Zhang Zhu. Chen Jicheng chaired the meeting and Shen Tilan recorded it. The research questions were: (1) The method of calculating and disclosing graduation grades. The result of the discussion was: A. Graduation grades are calculated by averaging the joint examination grades and school grades, each accounting for one-half. B. The method of disclosing graduation grades is based on the joint examination grades, but those who fail the joint examination but whose average with the school grades is passing should be noted. C. The standards for rewards and punishments for graduation grades are based on the joint examination grades, not the school grades. D. The current method of disclosing graduation grades should be revised as follows: (2) The ratio of students participating in the graduation joint examination to the number of graduation joint examinations and the number of omissions. Paper-based joint examination grades are counted without counting school grades. (3) The total average of the joint examination grades of students participating in the graduation joint examination in each school still follows the example of calculating the school joint examination grades and does not need to be calculated. (2) The temporary proposal submitted at the last meeting: whether the graduation joint examination system should continue to exist or be replaced by other methods. Shen Tilan advocated abolishing the joint examination system and replacing it with a random testing system. Xu Renhan advocated abolishing the joint examination system and replacing it with a national examination system. Jin Yuezhang advocated abolishing the joint examination system and seeking other methods to remedy it. (3) The date of the next meeting was set for 3:00 PM on May 8 at the Lakeside Club.

Training and Military Group

The Training and Military Group research meeting will be held at Lakeside Club at 2:00 PM this afternoon. The research questions are: (1) The content of the originally set training standards submitted at the last meeting, (2) The implementation methods of military management, (3) How to make school training permeate every student's actual life. Lin Meiyan will still be the chairman.

Track and Field Training Illustrations (1) 195

(Translated by Jiang Lianggui, not to be reproduced)

Mr. Jiang Lianggui has a lot of research on sports science and is currently teaching at the East Asia Sports College. He recently translated "Track and Field Training Method Illustrations" written by Robertson and Saki, coaches of the American track and field team at the 10th World Games. The article provides detailed analysis and illustrations for the entry methods, practice points, and the application of mechanics for each track and field event, supplementing the lack of text and making it easy for readers to compare the text and illustrations at a glance. With the track and field season approaching, we will disclose it daily in this column. We hope readers will pay attention to it (Editor's Note).

(1) Javelin

The javelin is one of the ancient sports. In the past, people used it as a weapon in warfare. In modern times, it has become one of the sports. Athletes who want to practice this sport must have considerable speed and a developed and healthy upper body with sensitive neurological responses. Of course, the javelin is the same as other sports. Those with tall stature have considerable convenience, but they must also have superior speed and the ability to fully coordinate the muscles of various parts of the body to assist them. It is not enough to rely solely on physical strength.

There are two methods of throwing the javelin, depending on the gait.

(A) Crossover Step

(Figure 1) The above picture shows the posture of the javelin thrower when moving forward. Athletes can gain experience to determine whether the steps they take are appropriate. Each practice should be measured in advance to develop a habit of fixed steps, so as not to have the disadvantage of disordered steps during the competition.
