Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 196

— (Master of Qifeng Tower)

Bismarck of Germany once said; "What we rely on today is only white iron and red blood." How majestic and thorough these words are, but the cruel policy of ambitious people has been completely exposed!

"Failure is the mother of success." This is to encourage people to continue to study diligently after a failure in a matter, and continue to study tirelessly, and there will naturally be a day to achieve success. If they are discouraged by failure, then the saying "mother of success" is equal to nonsense!

What parents give is love, and what lovers give is love. If we compare it with fruits, then love is like a peach, and love is like a Buddha's hand. Peaches are the most delicious and edible, but they will rot after a while. Although Buddha's hands are for people to play with and smell, they become dry and fragrant and do not dissipate.

Tea Picking 197

— Zhu Shaofei

Before the silkworm business is busy at home, tea leaves are a small product during this period. The whole family is busy picking, drying, and selling them for money. Part of the household expenses has to be subsidized by the money sold in this barren spring season.

Every garden of fruit trees is planted with lush tea trees. It can be said that no one in the village can compare with the lushness of my family's tea trees. People standing inside picking tea cannot be seen from the outside. These are all the hard work of my grandmother over the past few decades. She always cares with experience; fertilizing with firewood ash once a year, and how to cut off the old branches to make new buds sprout from the roots.

When I was a child, I was very happy because my small hands and feet could pick quickly, and I could always pick more than adults, so I would often be prevented from going to school for more than ten days in a row.

Every morning, I would follow my grandmother, mother, and sister JIn, with bamboo baskets hanging around their necks, to the mountain to pick tea. We smiled happily, dragged our light steps, and the dew on the spring grass stained our shoes and socks. We listened to the pleasant birdsong in the forest, and watched the eastern morning sun gradually rise higher.

When picking tea, the mothers would always talk about things that I had never heard at home, but I would sing out-of-tune mountain songs alone.

This scene seems like a moment in time, and now I am already the father of two children. Grandmother passed away five years ago. Sister Jin could pick tea, but was frightened by a snake touching her fingers on the tree, and died of a serious illness. Every year when the tea market is about to fall, my mother always cries with swollen eyes on the day of Sister Jin's death anniversary.

Now, these lush tea trees can only be picked by my mother alone, getting up early and grinding late. After picking in this garden, the tea buds in that garden have already "fired", so the tea buds that are picked and dried are not as fine as those of others and cannot be sold for a good price.

Pickpocketing Like a King 198

— Rongyu

"Pickpocketing Like a King" is a Hangzhou dialect phrase, equivalent to the Shanghai expression "knocking someone for a bamboo pole" and the Northern saying "extorting." People from other places may not understand other Hangzhou phrases, but they will always learn and comprehend the phrase "Pickpocketing Like a King."

"Everyone fears being pickpocketed like a king," but outsiders visiting Hangzhou inevitably get pickpocketed to some extent. It's understandable, as Hangzhou's economy relies on the three spring months. If they don't pickpocket those visiting playboys, young ladies, and wives, or those devout female believers wearing yellow cloth bags and chanting Amitabha, how would they survive drinking the northwest wind?

On the other hand, in recent years, Hangzhou has been designated as a national scenic area, and significant progress has been made in all aspects of construction. The bad habit of "pickpocketing like a king" has been reduced considerably. In the past, tourists in Hangzhou were most likely to be "pickpocketed like a king" when hiring boats, cars, and sedan chairs. Now, the Hangzhou government has set fixed prices and posted them in prominent places, allowing outsiders to know the rates at a glance and avoid being deceived. For example, renting a small boat to row on the lake used to cost five or six yuan, or even ten or eight yuan, per day. Now, the price is fixed at one yuan and fifty cents per day, one yuan for half a day, and two cents per hour, which is very convenient for people. As for food, due to the economic downturn, restaurants offer budget-friendly set meals, which are fixed and don't allow for pickpocketing. As for accommodation, hotels sell at fixed prices during these months, which are cheaper than Shanghai, but the extras can still be as expensive as in Shanghai.

People who go to Hangzhou always like to buy some local Hangzhou products, such as Zhang Xiaoquan's scissors, Shu Lianji's fans, and Wang Yutai's tea. These are brand-name products and won't be overpriced. However, if you buy lotus root powder, Chinese nutmeg, olives, etc., you need to be careful, or you might get "pickpocketed like a king."

— Juanyin

Cosmetic surgery, starting a new life, sweeping away funding.

Small Western Paradise 199

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 12: Ashamed of Being Unclothed, He Avoids Guests Behind a Curtain; Diligently Saves Lamp Oil, Transcribing Books at Dawn

He heard that I was there to visit and looked at what I was wearing from head to toe. He suspected I was an investigator from the provincial committee checking on their performance, so he quickly went inside to report, inviting the principal and teachers out. Logically, the students should all be old, and the teachers should be an old man, right? But what came out was another surprise. The principal was only in his twenties, and the teachers were not much older. I explained my intentions to them. The principal was very modest, saying there was nothing worth seeing. I said that I wanted to introduce the difficult situation of running education in the interior to the outside world to gain support from the people of the country. Seeing my sincere attitude, he led me inside. There is no need to describe the simplicity of the entire organization. Once we sat down to talk, I learned that the entire school, inside and out, consisted of only the principal and one teacher. There was also a handyman who took care of everything, including the gatekeeping and cooking. Because it was an ancient temple, there were three classrooms. However, a group of students around twenty years old were not in the classrooms attending class. Each held a copy of a thousand-character text, some wandering in the courtyard, some reciting aloud under the eaves. Some were reciting "It does not matter how high, as long as there is a fairy, it will be famous." Others were reciting "Mencius saw King Hui of Liang, and the king said, 'Old man.'" There were also two children of eight or nine years old, jumping and shouting, reciting "Camel, cart. Satchel, horse, cow." It turned out they were reciting picture recognition words used in kindergarten. Even if it was considered an improved private school, something was off. They shouldn't be running around the courtyard to read, so what was the point of the classrooms? Zhou Yourong laughed: "I've been a county magistrate in Shaanxi for almost a year, but I didn't know that education in the interior was like this." How bad was the order, and how did the principal react to you? Zhiqian said: "I think they are probably used to it and don't find it strange." (193)

Records of Incense and Whispers from the Imperial Court 200

— Original work by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

No matter the craft, a novice is never used; every newcomer must first immerse themselves in learning, and only after years of study will they have the opportunity to work. As for the leading artisans, it is even more difficult! Before becoming leaders, they must have years of outstanding achievements before being promoted. At the same time, their assistants must constantly strive to prepare for future promotion to leadership. As long as the original leader is older and no longer capable of performing well, a new leader is selected from the group of assistants who have been trained for many years to fill the position. Therefore, their craftsmanship will never decline, and they all have a consistent spirit and secret, like a hereditary profession passed down from father to son. Although in reality, they all have different backgrounds, with little blood or kinship between them, their spirit is like that of a family, which is different from the outside world!

Looking back now, the expenses within the palace were indeed enormous. Just from these crafts alone, it was enough to scare people to death. I lived in the palace for so many years, and I can say that not a day went by without new phoenix shoes being made and sent to the Empress Dowager for her to evaluate and inspect. At least one or two pairs, and up to five or six pairs, were sent every day. The accumulated number over a month or a year was naturally very large, and the amount of this expense was imaginable—but this was not surprising, because shoes were still a small thing. What was even stranger was that those large palace robes and embroidered clothes were also produced just as wastefully. (303)

Fallen Petal Season 201

— Ziwei

Flowers belong to the feminine realm. Throughout history, scholars and poets have often used flowers to symbolize women, as a shadow of women, because all flowers are delicate, weak, and unable to withstand the wind and rain. Once they are blown off, they fall to the ground, to be trampled on. The blooming and falling of flowers is only a matter of a few days of glory, a flash in the pan, fleeting, just like the life encounters of ill-fated beauties. Therefore, flowers have become confidantes of boudoirs, and women ultimately love flowers.

I remember in "Dream of the Red Chamber," Lin Daiyu, seeing fallen petals all over the ground with no one to sweep them, thought of the fragility of life and wrote "The Burial of Flowers," comparing herself to fallen flowers separated from their branches. She even felt that people were inferior to flowers.

"Fallen Petal Season," when cuckoos cry blood, is a season of common sorrow.

Now, there is a new film from a star, named "Fallen Petal Season," which is a poetic title, and the content must be very sad.

"Fallen Petal Season" tells the story of a woman who is hurt by spring, deceived by others, and wants to free herself, but in this male-dominated society, she will be met with obstacles. Not only is there no sympathetic assistance, but there are also people who ridicule and play with her—criticizing her—the result is that she suffers injustice and dies of illness. Although this is a fictional film, it is indeed a common occurrence in today's society. Who should be responsible for improving this situation in society?

Is the fate of women always as weak as flowers, easily stained with mud by the wind, and sinking?

Flower Protection Method 202

— (Wei Yuan)

If you want to take flowers to another place, it is best to wrap them in wet newspaper first, and then in dry newspaper. The end of the stem can be rolled tightly, and the other end should be looser. This can extend the life of the flowers.

After the flowers are brought to their destination, they should be immersed in a bucket of water, and short-stemmed flowers should be placed in a bowl.

Only change the water in the vase, don't add more. Adding a little salt to the water will keep the flowers bright.

Small Recipes

Spring Cuisine 203

— Zhu Yi

Seasonal Vegetables: In spring, all kinds of plants are just sprouting and growing. In terms of food, it is only good to eat the tender buds of vegetables. At this time, they are all on the market for meals, such as wolfberry shoots, aster scaber, toon shoots, etc., all of which are excellent vegetarian dishes, each with its own unique flavor. At this time of the Qingming Festival, the Taichi pond vegetables are picked for their fine buds and mixed with ham, tender bamboo shoots, shredded chicken, etc., and cooked into a soup. The greasy and fresh taste is truly unique. No wonder Mr. Zhang Jiying wanted to give up his official position and go home to eat pond vegetable soup.

Fish Soup: The pond fish in spring (Suzhou vulgar name, shape similar to the loach) is the most beautiful fresh fish for cooking soup. The fresh and tender fish meat, especially the two unique live pieces of meat on the fish cheeks, about the size of broad beans, are particularly delicious. When cooking the soup, first remove the fish skin, then remove the fish bones, and then cook with tender bamboo shoots and ham in chicken broth. The fresh and clean taste is truly the best appetizer. In spring, the fish meat is also unusually fresh and tender. Cooking soup with ham and tender bamboo shoots is also exceptionally delicious. Adding a little vinegar to the fish soup has a unique flavor.

Soft-shelled Turtle: Soft-shelled turtle is a common name. The soft-shelled turtles in spring are all small juveniles, and the meat and skirt are very tender. Therefore, when the cole flowers are yellow and the peonies are in bloom, soft-shelled turtles are very precious, called cole flower turtles and peony turtles, and the price is very expensive. To cook soft-shelled turtle, first kill the turtle (those with a red belly are poisonous, you should choose those with a white belly), cut the abdomen with a knife, peel off the black skin on the outside in boiling water, and then wash it clean in clear water. Braised or stewed soft-shelled turtle both have wonderful flavors. However, soft-shelled turtle, like "wearing armor," must be cooked with pork. Only by using the fat oil of pork will it be greasy and delicious to eat. The seasonings for braised soft-shelled turtle should be slightly sweet. The best part of the soft-shelled turtle is the skirt around the body, which is fat and tender. Eating it is truly delicious.

Chicken and Eel: Stewed chicken and eel is also a seasonal delicacy in spring. Kill and wash the fat yellow eel, cut it into small pieces, then cut the raw chicken into small pieces, and slowly stew them with ham and tender bamboo shoots over low heat. When the cooking is done, the taste of the chicken and eel is very delicious. Especially the clear soup, clear to the bottom, is more fresh and clean than any other dish.

Bamboo Shoot Oil: After the rain, there are countless spring bamboo shoots. Bamboo shoots are the most common vegetables in spring. The advantage of bamboo shoots is that whether they are cooked with meat, cooked vegetarian, seasoned, or cooked alone, they have their own unique flavor. In addition to cooking vegetables, bamboo shoots can also be used to make oil. To cook bamboo shoot oil, first cut the bamboo shoots into small pieces, heat a large pot of oil, and when the oil is hot, pour the bamboo shoots into the oil and slowly cook them until they are cooked. Then add soy sauce and cook until cooked. After that, put it in a ceramic jar and store it through the summer. This kind of bamboo shoot oil is fresh and fragrant and is a wonderful vegetarian product. Adding a few spoonfuls of bamboo shoot oil when eating noodles is truly no less delicious than mushroom oil!

Fourth Attempt to Pass Through the Threshold; Call Loan Rate Rises to 18% 206

For days, the silver market faced the difficult challenge of "four thresholds," severely impacting the money market. Although the major banks worked hard to maintain stability and avert crisis, it is undeniable that the vitality of the market has been significantly weakened. Yesterday, long-term rollovers faced challenges. Creditors wanted to collect, but debtors could not pay, resulting in further extensions. Both sides experienced considerable difficulty. Due to tight money conditions, the foreign call loan rate rose, reaching 18% in both morning and afternoon sessions, up 3% from the previous day. "Hua Tou Jia Shui" (premium for urgent transfers) also rose beyond 20%. Interbank call loan transactions were rare in the small clearing house, except for those with special relationships. Therefore, recent inflows and outflows were limited. Morning rollovers totaled over 2.8 million, with new transactions exceeding 400,000. Afternoon transactions exceeded 200,000. Transactions in the small clearing house amounted to 700,000. Foreign mortgage redemptions exceeded 500,000, with new short-term loans reaching 2.45 million. Customer deposits amounted to 400,000, and withdrawals were 300,000. Regarding banknote transactions, over 900,000 were collected, and 1.89 million were issued. Bank clearing operations showed foreign banks clearing over 3.34 million in banknotes, over 6.45 million in various goods and foreign exchange mortgages, over 780,000 in special remittances, over 1.22 million in foreign settlements, over 2 million in settlements, and 600,000 in warehouse entries. Chinese banks cleared over 3 million in banknotes, over 6.89 million in various loans and taxes, over 1.1 million in special remittances, over 1.56 million in foreign settlements, and 300,000 in warehouse entries. Japanese banks cleared over 2.23 million in banknotes, over 4.3 million in various goods and foreign exchange mortgages, over 1.56 million in foreign exchange settlements, over 900,000 in special remittances, and 800,000 in warehouse entries. Money shops cleared over 28 million in foreign public bills, over 5.8 million in foreign transfers, over 600,000 in various exchange bills, and over 1 million in cash conversions.

Since the financial crisis, little attention has been paid to the auxiliary currency market. Consequently, market prices have lacked intense competition, with only slight fluctuations. Yesterday, the Jiangjiao coin market appeared to decline slightly in the morning session, falling to 832 yuan per tael, but rebounded by 2.5 yuan in the afternoon to 834.5 yuan. Transactions in the morning session totaled 3,000 coins, and 6,000 coins in the afternoon session. Guangdong small silver dollars were priced at 734.3 yuan in the morning session, dropping slightly by 0.8 yuan to 733.5 yuan in the afternoon. Transactions in the morning session totaled 215,000 coins, and 35,000 coins in the afternoon session. Copper coins remained unchanged at 337,000, with 43,040 strings traded, equivalent to 12,000 yuan in silver dollars.

Securities: Public Bonds Slightly Recover Due to Short Covering 207

Gold Short Bonds Particularly Strong: Up 45 Jiao

Yesterday, the Chinese Securities Exchange saw a slight improvement due to a somewhat positive environment. There were expectations of changes in the U.S. silver purchase policy, the potential passage through the "four thresholds" crisis, closer relations between China and Japan, and no decline in Shanghai's silver reserves, but rather an increase. Confidence strengthened, and the market improved due to short covering. Market conditions revealed a substantial number of short positions, mostly held by large investors. Whether they needed to cover was uncertain. The market trend could be described as robust, with gold short bonds being the most sought-after. War bonds appeared weak in comparison. Previously, war bonds were 3-4 yuan higher than gold short bonds, but now gold short bonds are over 1 yuan higher than war bonds. This phenomenon clearly indicates that many are abandoning war bonds in favor of gold short bonds. This is because gold short bonds offer better terms than war bonds and have a shorter maturity. With a little research, the advantages and disadvantages are obvious. The trend is expected to gradually shift. If the environment remains unchanged, prices should rise. Yesterday, at the opening of the morning session, various factions gradually increased their buying interest, with No. 48 being particularly active in purchasing, while No. 52 sold significantly. Prices rose by 0.15-0.45 yuan. In the second session, the front rows continued to rise by 0.2-0.3 yuan, while the back rows were slightly weaker. At the opening of the afternoon session, prices were mostly stable, slightly improving by around 0.1 yuan. At the close, the bulls showed some profit-taking, with a slight decline of around 0.1 yuan, but this did not indicate a downward trend. Overall, prices rose, ranging from 0.1 to 0.3 yuan, with gold short bonds rising by 0.4-0.5 yuan. The total transaction volume was 6.47 million yuan. Yarn and Cotton: Delivery Results of Marked Yarn and Cotton 209

Yarn Price at 182 Yuan...Volume 2,900 Bales; Cotton Price at 34.5 Yuan...Volume 4,000 Bales

The April Gold Rooster brand yarn contract, listed on November 1st of last year, opened at 183.6 yuan, slightly declining to 182.2 yuan. Subsequently, Mr. Wu and several other influential individuals took long positions, fueled by market rumors of potential inflationary policies in China. Sentiment soared, and buying interest was strong, reaching a peak of 189.6 yuan. However, the Shanghai financial crisis at the end of the lunar year caused significant panic, with bank closures and runs on money shops, creating an extremely serious situation that severely impacted commerce. At the beginning of the spring season, the market abruptly reversed. By March 12th, American cotton had plummeted over 100 points. Adding insult to injury, market conditions became even more difficult to sustain, breaking through the 180 yuan mark. Fortunately, local yarn was still in high season, with spring sales developing.

Customer demand was still strong, with purchases arriving from southern ports. Yarn inventories at various factories gradually decreased, from over 70,000 bales to over 60,000 bales. Therefore, despite the poor environment, the actual situation remained relatively stable. Mr. Wu insisted on taking delivery, causing prices to rebound above 180 yuan, reaching a high of 183.9 yuan. More recently, due to the money market panic at the end of April, along with deliveries from inland factories, the market suffered a severe blow, falling back to 180.3 yuan. However, the long positions prepared to buy, and the final session remained firm at 183 yuan. As a result, 2,900 bales remained, with only 550 bales of 16-count "Earth" brand yarn delivered. The rest were settled through self-delivery at a price of 182 yuan. The broker codes and bale quantities for both the receiving and delivering parties are listed below: (Unit: Bales)

Seller Delivering

Tong Ji: 550 Sui Long: 200 Ming De: 50

Shen Ji: 500 Ren Feng: 50 Yi Chang: 100

Run Kang: 100 Xin Cheng: 350 De Ji: 50

Heng Yi: 50

Buyer Receiving

Yu Da: 800 He Xing: 50 Shen Chang: 1,000

Chang Feng: 50

The April marked cotton contract, listed on November 1st of last year, opened at 36.15 yuan, declining to 35.85 yuan. However, Tong Cheng Co. and some cotton merchants aggressively bought, driving up prices. At the same time, rumors of currency reform circulated in the market, boosting confidence and attracting buyers. While cotton stocks piled up in the Northwest, spot traders showed strong interest in hoarding, and banks invested heavily, anticipating a price increase in the coming spring, reaching a peak of 38.75 yuan. However, during the settlement period, the money market experienced a major panic, with bankruptcies occurring frequently and extremely tight credit conditions. At the beginning of spring, overseas silver prices rose sharply, while gold fell. Foreign cotton became cheaper to import, and prices declined sharply. Banks and cotton merchants, facing economic hardship and unstable yarn factories, rushed to sell, exacerbating the situation. Market sentiment was difficult to sustain, and on March 12th, American cotton plunged by over 100 points. The fragile cotton market suffered a further blow, falling into a slump. The lowest price reached 33.05 yuan, but the long position of Mr. Shao held firm, with a strong intention to buy, and prices rebounded to 35.4 yuan. More recently, deliveries were sufficient, but the sharp rise in silver prices caused a dramatic drop in gold, leading to a decline in market sentiment and a drop back to 34.30 yuan. As a result, 6,000 bales remained, including 4,000 bales of Shandong coarse cotton, Tianjin coarse cotton, and Yao cotton. The rest were settled through self-delivery at a price of 34.50 yuan, with Mr. Shao receiving the most. Grains: Flour Market Skyrockets by Four Points This Month 213

Forward Months Also Rise

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market, the prices for all months initially appeared stable, then gradually rose. Foreign wheat quotations from both Chicago and Canada rebounded slightly by two to three points. After the opening, due to low foreign wheat quotations and clear weather, short positions were initially released, with the opening price at only 4.45 jiao. Subsequently, short covering became active. Customer firms did not show any signs of releasing their positions. However, with delivery approaching, short positions had to be covered. Furthermore, pre-arranged shipments for customer firms had already been loaded, but the required standards had not yet been purchased. These factors contributed to a squeeze. Subsequent opening prices rose steadily. As for the forward months, spring droughts in Shandong Province and sandstorms in Pingjin caused the price of wheat to increase by three points, leading to strong market sentiment. At the opening of the afternoon session, prices were initially stable, but the current month became increasingly squeezed, with short covering continuing without limit. The highest price reached 5.075 jiao (over 6 points higher than the morning opening). Forward months continued to rise due to the current month's situation and limited factory selling. Given this situation, half of the reason is the need to increase spot flour prices, and the other half is the drought situation in Hebei Province, which suggests that there is no hope for a price decline in the short term. As a result, the current month rose by 4 points, May rose by 3.25 points, June rose by 2.7 points, July rose by 3.2 points, August rose by 2.7 points, and September rose by 2.25 points. Old wheat arrivals continued.

Old Wheat Arrivals Continue; No Expectation of Excessive Price Increase 214

After the opening of the wheat futures market yesterday, prices for all months remained stable. Foreign wheat quotations from Chicago and Canada fell back by about three points. Although Pingjin faced sandstorms and Shandong Province reported early droughts, new wheat was expected to arrive in Jiangnan in about 20 days. Furthermore, old wheat from the Yangtze River, nearing its replacement, was arriving smoothly, with daily imports of around 10,000 bales. Due to the influx of spot goods, market sentiment remained calm, with gains of only two to three points, unlike the surge in the flour market. Transactions in the afternoon session were not very active, and prices fluctuated. In the long run, with old goods continuing to arrive, there is no reason for excessive price increases. As a result, July and August each rose by two points, while September rose by three points. The spot wheat market, due to abundant arrivals, saw stable high prices and weaker medium to low prices. Kaifeng Shandong Guiding wheat was priced at 3.95 yuan, Yingzhou Bengbu wheat at 3.93 yuan, Luohe wheat at 3.89 yuan, and Hankou wheat at 3.878 yuan. A total of 9,000 bales were handled by Che Feng.

River Rice

The source of supply of Shanghai's rice merchants is slightly more plentiful, with arrivals on the 26th and 27th (a total of over 5,000 stones). Prices for various grades of Hou Geng (glutinous rice) and late rice declined. Yin Bian (cloudy variation) was rare and remained stable. Trading was active yesterday, and prices have been rising by 3-5 fen. 客秈's (Customer Xian rice) trading was limited, and the market remained stable, but sellers were mostly optimistic and unwilling to easily sell their goods.

Unfavorable exchange rates and stagnant silk sales have led domestic silk shops to successively close due to economic conditions. Currently, only Meiya and two other companies are still operating, and even those are only working part-time. Demand for user silk is also declining. Few silk factories in Shanghai are still open (only Jiyu Maitai and two other silk factories). The silk industry is becoming increasingly pessimistic this spring. Today, 30 bales of Qilihuijing were imported by Kailiyanghang.

Qimen Black Tea Skyrockets 219

According to a telegram from Qimen, the price of raw tea has skyrocketed from 80 yuan to 105 yuan due to the large number of buyers. The cost of manufacturing and transporting it to Shanghai in the future will be over 200 yuan.

Local Estate's New Green Tea Now Available 220

Yesterday, the Zhenmei green tea produced by local tea factories was released by Shenyuan Tea Shop. It is said that this new tea is from Zhuang tea in Shangyu, Zhejiang Province, and the quality is good. However, European tea companies are mostly taking a wait-and-see attitude due to the recent increase in overseas silver prices and the poor wheat harvest in Morocco this year, which has significantly reduced farmers' purchasing power. Only Xiehe Tianyu and other firms offered 60-70 yuan, which is 70% lower than last year's opening price and far from the cost of Chinese merchant arrivals, so no transactions were made.

Sui'an New Tea Rises Opportunistically 221

Sui'an is a key tea-producing area in Zhejiang Province, producing approximately 8,000 dan annually. Its convenient transportation and relatively low manufacturing costs have attracted attention. In recent years, with the global economic downturn, foreign firms have favored cheaper teas, making Sui tea suitable for the needs of buyers. Therefore, while tea businesses in Anhui and Jiangxi Provinces have suffered significant losses in the past two years, Sui tea has been less affected. In the past, there were only nine tea firms in the county, but in the past four or five years, the number has increased to over twenty. Furthermore, tea firms in Shanghai and Hangzhou, which used to purchase Chun'an and Kaihua teas as raw materials, are now mostly switching to Sui tea, leading to increased sales. The new tea in the county has already sprouted. The mountain households in the southwest townships of Yaping, Dayuan, Xiyuan, Fenglin, and Fenkou, in order to produce high-quality tea and avoid price reductions from the firms, have started picking and processing tea earlier this year. In the past two days, many gardens have already opened. Tea firms are rushing to transport the new tea to Shanghai to be the first to market, and have sent staff to weigh and buy the tea. The future opening price is not expected to be lower than last year.

The Advantage of Hunan Red Tea Remains Prominent 222

Hunan has always been a region rich in tea production, especially with red tea accounting for the largest export volume. Although it has been hit by sluggish foreign sales in recent years, the market has narrowed. However, since the restoration of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, the sales of Hunan tea to Russia have shown signs of recovery. In addition, the provincial authorities are working hard to revive the local tea industry, and the market is gradually improving. This year, new tea from Anhua, Xinhua, Taoyuan, Pingjiang, and Liuyang counties has already entered the market. Merchants from Jin, Yue, Hui, Han, and Shanghai, as well as local tea merchants, have flocked to the mountains to start their businesses. Money houses and tea firms in Hankou and Changsha are interested in investing and lending to tea companies, and the financial situation is quite flexible. It is estimated that there are more than one hundred foreign firms, tea firms, and tea companies this year. Junshan Guyu green tea and foreign firms' red tea Baihao have already been harvested one after another, and various companies are currently busy transporting funds and collecting tea. The market atmosphere is even more lively than last year.

Metals: Italian Double-Linked Iron Continues to Rise 223

Ninety-pound Italian double-linked iron: The market price rose by another twenty-five cents the day before yesterday, with each box priced at twenty-nine yuan and fifty cents. Only factories in this street are doing well, while merchants from other regions are just inquiring. According to investigations by foreign firms, very few goods have arrived recently, so the market still has a trend of further rise.

Free Talk

American Popular Songs After the Arrival of the Depression 224

— Sen

In 1929, the United States began an unprecedented depression. Countless factories closed down, and tens of thousands of people lost their jobs. The bridges of Boston became open-air hotels for the unemployed masses. The veterans petitioning outside New York City jokingly hung up the sign of a grand hotel in Chicago outside their dilapidated tents. Groups of unemployed people reached out to the White House for bread. - These sufferings were all reflected in their popular songs at the time, which became a mirror of the disaster of that suffering.

When this suffering first arrived, the happy "Yankees" (a common term for Americans) began to feel unhappy. So, the street poets who were starving also wrote countless unhappy songs. The most popular at the time was a song called "Give Yourself a pat on the back." As soon as this song came out, countless people who failed in the market sang like this:

"Smile and be happy!

For tomorrow we can't count the breaches of contract,

Let's mortgage it to him!"

This is a gloomy song of forced laughter in the era of depression. On the contrary, there is a bit of optimistic atmosphere in "Let's have another cup of coffee."

"The rainbow is now in the sky,

Let me have another cup of coffee!

Let me eat another meat bun!"

The depression of 1932 was even more severe, and more popular songs about the depression were produced. The most common were "Good times are coming so cheer up" and "Happy days are here again."

These are exactly a reflection of the "Yankee boy's" unyielding spirit, but the depression was too profound. When they couldn't bear it, they finally produced naked and desolate melancholic popular songs. The first to appear was "Brother, can you spare a dime?" From this time on, the street poets wrote truthfully and consistently. At that time, news of local bank closures was spreading everywhere in the United States, and sighs of unemployment were heard everywhere. In a popular song, there was a line that said:

"It's Monday,

I still only have a dime!" Everyone was oppressed by poverty and hunger, and humming "I still only have a dime" was indeed the most palatable sentimental line.

From 1932 to 1933, the dark clouds were still low. Hundreds of thousands of people who were once able to live a decent life fell into poverty, and the unemployment rate continued to rise. After these street poets were temporarily silent, they couldn't easily wait for an optimistic era to arrive, so they produced gloomy tunes like "Turn out the lights and go to sleep!"

"There's no more money in the bank!

There are no naughty children for us to spank!

What should we do after all?

Turn out the lights and go to sleep!"

This is almost a song sung with tears. It is indeed a strange phenomenon that the people of the optimistic, naturally blessed golden country would encounter such difficulties and be so heartbroken!

But Americans are not fatalists and will not always be so sad. As the economic situation improved slightly, they immediately became optimistic again. At the end of 1933, songs like "The road is open again" and "The cheer parade" appeared.

Under President Roosevelt's recovery plan, grand popular songs like "Marching along together" were produced.

"Marching along,

Sharing smiles and tears,

Marching along,

Whistling that the sky will be clear." In the middle of this song, there are clearly still traces of material pain. Just like in another love song:

"Say, darling, do you have some money saved up?

That's all I need to know."

The poverty of overly utilitarian lovers is truly written humorously and vividly.

The short song that is currently sweeping across the United States, often used as a quote in politicians' speeches and major news articles, and makes everyone smile when they sing it, is the majestic "Who's afraid?"

"Who's afraid of the big bad wolf?

The big bad wolf,

The big bad wolf,

Who's afraid of this...?"

Currently, the entire United States is singing this song with the same majestic force as a battle song. Everyone is humming it in their mouths, as if they want to scare away the terrible wolf of depression with the singing of all the American people.

By observing the content of these songs in general, we know that what is expressed in them is very real emotion. In the middle, there is the unyielding Yankee, the anti-fatalistic optimism, but also the sigh of despair. - How sincere and frank these emotions are!

Life 225

— He Wei

Recently, my life has indeed been terrible. I have no certainty at all. I don't know if I will starve to death tomorrow. Living in a bathroom, I think about writing something to solve my life every day, but this hope is always slim, because once an article is written and sent out, there is no news from then on, and the so-called "hope" is over.

Although I rarely experience complete starvation, I taste the flavor of semi-starvation every day here. I eat a bowl of plain noodles for twelve copper coins each meal, plus two sesame cakes, which barely gets me by. Sometimes I just eat two sesame cakes.

Two-thirds of my day is spent borrowing money, regardless of the weather, whether it is cold winter or hot summer. Sometimes I wander on the road or by the river, sometimes I squeeze into third-class streetcars. When the weather is hot, I still drag around a tattered cotton robe. I am completely dazed and have lost consciousness. When I walk, I feel like I am floating in the air.

"Find a job!"

Friends kindly urge me. I think so myself, but the problem is this, because I am completely clueless about where to find a job. Every place is already full, and there is no room to stand. Sometimes I think it would be good to be a proofreader, but even this job that I used to despise a few years ago is so difficult.

It is strange how I have been able to live until now. According to many people's calculations, I should have died long ago, and even my bones should have already withered. But I am still able to live today, which makes many friends happy on the one hand, and makes many friends embarrassed on the other.

"You don't work, and you don't have any articles published. How do you live by borrowing a little money? You are really capable, really amazing!"

Most of these friends are very surprised. They carefully examine me, interrogate me, show suspicious faces, and grin with their white teeth.

"I don't believe it, maybe you are being supported by someone..."

Because they want to dance, watch plays, go to fancy restaurants, and even gamble, they naturally cannot understand my kind of life. They can't understand, but they shamelessly spread rumors, which I will never forget.

What is even more infuriating is that after many friends learned about my predicament, they retorted me as if I were lying:

"But your clothes are still quite clean!"

The meaning is that if I were really as embarrassed as you say, then I would undoubtedly be as filthy and ragged as a beggar. My current clothes seem a bit too dignified.

But my dear friends! I am not a beggar after all...

Mr. Kapitan (Part 1) 226

— Hei Ying

"Child, let me tell you: to live, you must risk your life. Do you think there is no danger if there are no wild boars? You are wrong. People sometimes eat people!" Leaving home, sitting in the third-class carriage filled with the smell of red betel nuts and the white mist of Elephant brand cigarettes, I, alone, was on my way back to that Western-style clothing store, remembering my father's words. The train wheels rumbled forward, and the car body swayed slightly. Sticking my head out, the world outside the window was vast.

More than two hours later, I arrived at the small pier where I had to get off. I jumped off the train with a large package on my back, which contained the necessities for a person's life. I didn't have the money to take a carriage, and it would take at least thirty minutes to walk to my destination.

I walked. The sun, which is always June-like, shone on my head, and two streams of sweat rolled down my forehead. Clenching my teeth, I was prepared to suffer some hardships on the journey of life and return here again.

"Ah, it's you? Why are you back again?" The boss came up to me, seemingly surprised, and asked.

I put down my package, panting, "Dad wanted me to come back, so—" I looked at the boss's pig-like face. He took a breath, touched his lips with his hand, and said to me, "You can live here." So, I carried my package back up to the dark and cramped little room on the third floor. I was just about to sit down on the hard bed board to rest when someone downstairs called my name.

It was the boss's wife. Her oily pockmarked face appeared on the stairs. This woman handed the grocery basket to me and, without waiting for me to ask, rattled off what she wanted to buy; at the same time, she gave me the money that should be paid to the pork stall or the vegetable stand, and walked away swaying her hips.

Life returned to the way it was before. The clerk who collected accounts recovered from his illness, and he still went out every day on that bicycle. "I'd be happy to encounter a wild boar once," he once said to me, "I don't know how many gardens and wildernesses I've walked through, but I haven't been able to see them." As if very disappointed, this guy shook his head. People who have never felt the dangers of life do not understand hardship - In the evening, when I finished everything I had to do and dragged my tired body up to the third floor, hiding in that dark corner to rest, I thought to myself. If he really met a wild boar one day, he would definitely be scared out of his wits!

During this period, my apprenticeship was hard and lonely. Especially in the evenings, the tailors all went outside after dinner. Everyone seemed to be able to find their place. For example, the clerk who collected accounts went to the coffee shop on the back street every night, mingled with those Hainanese people, and talked wildly until it was time to sleep before coming back. I was not allowed to leave: and I was not allowed to close the store door until half past nine. So, I often sat blankly at the store door, looking at the lonely street. The Javanese in the barbershop across the street would sit at the door and play a Japanese-made six-stringed guitar when he was happy, or sing; the sound broke through the monotony of the street. Following this singing, from time to time, a middle-aged man would come to our house, always sitting on the chair next to the tailor's table with his thin body, not saying much. He seemed to have a good relationship with the boss, and they would talk non-stop until it was time to close the door.

"Mr. Kapitan," I turned my head and said to him. My Amoy dialect was not very good. I tried my best to speak to the extent that he could understand: "The boss has gone out." I pointed to the street outside, and at this moment a carriage was passing by.

Life 227

— Zhou Lengjia

Like a heavily loaded camel, traveling in the desert.

My heart longs for a green millet, but there is no mirage of an oasis in sight.

Like a sturdy whip, held in the hand of the Creator.

It whips my heart day and night, making my heart hurt and sad.

After Childbirth 228

— Hu Xu

Like me, my friend Li, who is down on his luck in a foreign land, sent me a letter this morning, telling me: "Yesterday at dusk, our daughter came out of her mother's womb, covered in blood, into this chaotic world! Now, both the big and the small are safe; but because we have no money, we didn't even prepare clothes for the child beforehand, so our poor child is still lying naked in the tattered quilt as I write this letter. Can you find a way to get some money to save our child!"

Money, I felt in my pocket and there were only twenty-six copper coins left, which is the money for today's meal. "That's it," I calculated in my heart. People with no money have to be pathetic; "I'll go get some children's clothes for him."

I lowered my head and walked out of my own dwelling. Avenue Joffre was long and smooth, the dull sky pressed on my head, and the wind was fanning around me, but my heart was almost scorching with heat.

At the intersection of Rue Luber, I found the residence of my fellow villager Su. Su and his wife were happily dressing their two-year-old little angel in exquisite and gorgeous new clothes in the delicate bedroom. When they saw me, they greeted me as if to confirm the joy in their hearts.

"Come and see how beautiful our child is?"

I nodded blankly, and then said in a tone that surprised them:

"I want to ask you for a favor!"

"What do you want?" the man asked.

"Can you give me a few of the clothes that your child wore when he was first born?"

"Did you have a child?" the woman said jokingly, which made my fellow villager Su, who was staring with doubtful eyes, laugh too.

"No," I said, "It's a poor friend of mine."

"Sure," the man said generously to his wife; "Go get a few for me."

Waiting, red and green children's clothes were handed over from the wardrobe, from the hands of the female benefactor, one piece, two pieces... "Here are ten pieces," the woman said, "They are still very new, but don't forget the red eggs."

What senseless words. If I could afford to send red eggs, what would I be worried about children's clothes! But I certainly thought it was unnecessary to explain to them; this was enough for me to be grateful for. I said goodbye with a thousand thanks, and I felt much lighter! The dull sky was far away from me, the wind brought a pleasant breath, and every street was bustling with happy people.

Route Tenant de la Tour passed under my excited steps; I arrived, the narrow kitchen where my friend Li lived arrived. Li's back was to the door, bending over to the old woman lying on the pit! His wife seemed to be discussing something.

"Oh, Lao Wu is here!"

The first to see me were the woman's two absent-minded eyes, followed by my friend Li's face, which was always depressed, turning around.

"A Wu!"

We shook hands, and the boiling hot blood was exchanged in each other's palms. My sight shifted from his face to the pit;

"How is she?"

"Still - good." She spoke slowly and weakly, followed by a aggrieved smile on the corners of her anemic mouth.

"I've already got the child's clothes." I opened the clothing bag; "Ten pieces in total, a fellow villager of mine gave them to me, and they are still 90% new."

The air flowed in the narrow kitchen.

"Take it, put it in the quilt to warm it up, and then you can put it on her. Lao Wu," she was happy; "Come and see the child!"

I could see clearly that there was a skinned frog in the tattered quilt!

"I have to go back," I said, "I'll try to get some money in a few days."

"It's best to get it before the end of the month, because the rent has already been asked for four times." the man said, there was no politeness between us.

"Okay."

I answered anxiously, dragging my heavy shackles as if I were leaving them, and the dull sky pressed on my head again! ...

Dance Marathon (7) 229

— (Written by American LT Earl) Translated by Yi Xian

After resting for some time, Tax joined other dance "Marathons," which became his profession. He obtained a translation of "Yes, We Have No Bananas" in Greek, and practiced the song. This song and his special dance later became very famous. The audience who liked this kind of song and dance gradually increased, and he could earn ten to fifteen dollars a day in extra money. Even if he had to withdraw from the "Marathon" on the field sometimes, when he withdrew, his pockets were still full of money. When he had a large batch of savings in the bank, he couldn't help but have the idea of returning to his hometown, just like a rich American. He is now a celebrity in this new world. He was entertained by famous Greek compatriots, and his photo was even placed on top of short articles in Greek newspapers.

Tax participated in a total of sixteen dance "Marathons." He received the top prize eight times, and he also won the "Super Marathon" trophy worth one thousand yuan. Only the winners of other "Marathons" could participate in this "Marathon," and there was no rest period during the dance. He now had five thousand yuan in savings, enough for him to return to his hometown, so he returned to Greece. However, the hard work of the previous "Marathons" had damaged his lungs, and he was suffering from tuberculosis. Several sanatoriums were opened in the mountains of his Greek hometown. When he returned to Greece, he had to become a patient in one of them. He lived there with rotten lungs, and the money he earned in the United States was just enough to cover his expenses. (End)

Supplement to the Shanghai Edition of Shenbao

Talks

Banning Coeducation 230

— Li Min

The issue of coeducation was once a major issue of contention in Chinese education and in society as a whole. Now, this issue seems to have come to an end, but now some people are trying to overturn this old case. According to reports, Peiping has decided to implement single-sex schools for middle schools and strictly prohibit coeducation from the 24th year of the Republic onwards. This issue has now been excavated from the old papers and placed before us again.

Regarding the issue of coeducation, there is actually nothing worth discussing in the content. In the eyes of those who consider themselves responsible for maintaining morality, this is nothing more than telling women that they must eventually return silently to the family - no, back to the cage of man-eating etiquette. This is not at all harsh. Upon careful examination of the hearts and minds of those who consider themselves responsible for maintaining morality, they believe that coeducation is the system that is most likely to destroy social morality and make the "order" of society even more difficult to maintain (because, in addition to men, a group of unsettled people has been added). As a result, no one is responsible for the old etiquette. In this way, we, who bear the responsibility of maintaining morality, cannot but rise up and pay attention to the issue of coeducation. Making women leave society, return to the family, and return to the tomb of old etiquette will surely make society much more peaceful.

There are many places around us where the many pains and oppressions should be discussed, but these will not be of any interest to those who bear the responsibility of maintaining morality. The extreme sharpening of social economy does not feel like a very cruel thing to them at all. They now seem to be focused on the issue of so-called morality. The cries from hell will immediately turn into a gentle breeze when they fly to their ears. On the contrary, they have not relaxed their efforts to maintain morality for a moment, which is truly admirable.

Driving the Yellow Ducks 231

— Ya Fei

As the morning sun first rises, the morning mist shyly dissipates; wisps of smoke already curl above the rooftops of many homes in Bright Moon Bay, enveloping this small fishing village in a haze, leaving only a blurred outline of the entire village. Besides the crowing of roosters, there are also the cries and fussing of children in the village; thus, the quiet air is suddenly filled with noise and bustle. The riverbank in front of the village is completely crowded with women washing rice and vegetables, their conversations and laughter noisily blending into one.

At this time, Old Fourth Yellow Duck had habitually slipped off the hard plank bed, let out a heavy cough, and dragged a damp smoking pipe towards the outhouse in the open space behind the house to relieve himself.

Returning, he wiped his face and saw that his wife had already cooked the leftover rice from the previous night into porridge, so he picked out a thicker piece of rice crust and took a big bowl—

After eating breakfast, he routinely went to the duck shed, opened the door; one, two, three... he counted the yellow ducks coming out of their nests, checking for any accidents, or perhaps signs of disease? Once all the yellow ducks had left the shed and gathered in the open space in the yard, vying to eat the wheat bran soaked in water, he carried a bamboo basket, squatted down, and reached one hand into the warm duck shed, feeling for white-shelled and greenish-shelled duck eggs, gently placing them in the basket. A stench of duck droppings drilled straight into his nostrils, but this was unavoidable for Old Fourth Yellow Duck.

One, two, three... ten... fifteen... twenty... thirty... thirty-one; he counted the eggs in the basket, there were thirty-one. He thought: thirty-one would have been worth a dollar in the early years when foreign goods were cheap and eggs were expensive: but, but, now they are one cent each, you'd need a hundred for a dollar, so thirty-one are only worth thirty cents or so. If each duck lays an average of one hundred eggs, then each duck makes only a dollar a year. If you calculate with fifty ducks (assuming nothing unexpected happens), you only make fifty dollars of income. How can fifty dollars be enough to support my family? Besides, the ducks still need to eat!

His wife walked over and took the egg basket.

"Be careful not to break them; there are thirty-one here!" He solemnly handed her the egg basket.

"Now we have more than a hundred eggs at home. You should take them to exchange for some rice! The rice has long been used up, and we should return the two sheng of rice we borrowed from Auntie San." She nagged at him.

"Oh!" He seemed indifferent as he answered and shouldered a herding pole, heading towards the river beach. When those yellow ducks saw the pole with a broken banana leaf fan hanging on the end, they climbed from the riverbank into the river, floating on the water.

The small boat gradually moved towards the corner of the bay: Old Fourth Yellow Duck stood at the bow of the boat with the herding pole across his shoulders, directing the duck flock on one hand and checking the riverbank on the other. The duck flock leisurely paddled on the water, following the direction of the herding pole, "Quack! Quack!" as they searched for small fish and shrimp in the river to fill their stomachs.

The sun slowly climbed from the east to the center of the sky, and all the fishing boats on the river returned one by one for lunch; the ducks' bellies were probably full, but Old Fourth Yellow Duck's stomach was rumbling, so he also herded the flock of ducks back for lunch. In the afternoon, he released them again until the sun hid behind the mountains, then he blocked their path with the herding pole, letting the ducks pass under the pole; one, two, three... he counted them like that.

Old Fourth Yellow Duck had been herding yellow ducks for more than ten years. Whether it was spring, summer, autumn, winter, or even on days with drizzling rain, his life was always on the river: except during wind, rain, ice, and snow, when he had to feed these ducks more than ten catties of bean dregs or bran, which was really difficult to manage. So he would start to worry whenever he encountered this kind of weather.

Crossing White Wave Shoal 232

— Tian Qi

——Random Notes on Returning South——

About half a li of water remained to reach White Wave Shoal when the boat docked by the dike. The boatman said it was time to ascend the shoal. Seven or eight towline pullers were already waiting on the dike. These pullers were all from mountain villages near White Wave Shoal, and they made a living pulling towlines year-round. Without these towline haulers, boats could not pass the shoal. According to the boatman, they were also divided into gangs. Each boat had a fixed employer, and they could not arbitrarily hire from other gangs. Usually, when the water level was low, boatmen only needed to pay one and a half or two dollars to tow the boat across the shoal; if the water was high, the price would increase to three or four dollars, all according to established rules.

The water at White Wave Shoal was treacherous, with turbulent waves and many hidden reefs, with only a winding waterway in the middle that was barely passable for boats. Boatmen on the Meijiang River felt anxious and fearful when they reached this point, considering it a matter of life and death. Therefore, passengers often preferred to disembark here, both to reduce the load and to avoid any possible danger.

It was noon, and I had been cooped up in the small cabin for half a day's journey, feeling extremely bored. Hearing that the boat was about to ascend the shoal, I suddenly thought it would be interesting to take the opportunity to go ashore and help them pull the towline. So, I quickly rummaged through my silk basket for my sneakers, stepped out of the boat, and explained to the boatman with a smile that I was going to help everyone pull the towline.

—It's very strenuous, sir. Anyway, the boat is lightly loaded, so it doesn't matter if you stay in the cabin. And the sun is very strong.

The boatman gave me a kindly wry smile, implying that I was someone who wouldn't even find it easy to walk a little in the sun.

—It doesn't matter! Just lend me a bamboo hat. Don't think of me as a weakling, I grew up in the countryside!

They laughed loudly and immediately grabbed a bamboo hat for me. Including the towline pullers and boatmen, there were twelve of us in total. After securing the towline, we stepped forward one by one, dragging the boat far behind us on the water, advancing towards the turbulent waves of the shoal.

The midday sun in June was like a ball of fire scorching our heads, and our bodies were drenched in sweat. When we dragged the boat to a cliff, the path suddenly became steep and narrow; the boat was close to the head of the shoal, and the water was becoming more rapid. The roar of the waves was like ten thousand horses galloping, and the towline on our shoulders was pulled even tighter; our feet felt like they were floating on the sand, never quite finding solid ground, and our steps gradually became heavy and sluggish. Perhaps fearing that I was overexerting myself, they shouted while gasping for air.

—Sir, put it down, the road is dangerous: falling would be no joke!

The road was indeed narrow and dangerous, and below the cliff was the turbulent stream of the shoal! But I wasn't afraid, my heart was surged with a tragic and excited blood! Looking at the surging, roaring stream, sweat flowed on my face, back, and hands! Forgetting my exhaustion, forgetting the danger, as if I had forgotten something, I suddenly remembered the movie "Volga River Comes." Looking back at the bent backs and ragged clothes of the towline haulers and boatmen on White Wave Shoal, I felt that they all shared the same poor existence and fate as the Volga boatmen! My heart felt weighed down, and I felt an infinite sadness rise within me. So, I gasped for air and opened my throat to sing the tragic and desolate boatmen's song.

This caused them to laugh comically. Of course, they wouldn't understand my feelings and thoughts at this moment; nor would they understand the meaning of this song. One of the boatmen asked.

—Sir, you're working hard, both towing and singing. What song are you singing? It sounds quite good.

—Sounds good? Eh?…….

The sun scorched their heads, and sweat flowed on their faces, backs, and bodies. They, understanding or not, didn't say a word, panting for breath, step by step, dragging their thick legs.

Execution 233

— Ke Qiu

Death on the Road 234

— Shi Ying

That morning, as usual, it was gloomy. I went downstairs, and they were talking about a passenger who had fallen to his death at the wharf. The wharf wasn't far from where I lived, and I had nothing to do anyway, so naturally I wanted to go take a look. The streets of the small town were muddy in the morning; a thin mist shrouded the river in a pale color. The early morning steamship had already departed, but the wharf was still unusually bustling, with a circle of people gathered, their voices floating with noise. From the crowd, I saw a middle-aged man lying stiffly on the cold, wet cobblestones. He was already stiff and cold. A paper umbrella and a white package lay beside him, and his withered, straight arm still seemed to be reluctantly clutching at them. His face, as wooden as dead ashes, seemed to have much more to say; even if he could speak, who would he tell? All around were faces filled with curiosity and gloating, and the occasional shallow sigh was quickly covered by the hubbub of conversation and banter. Only the stiff man lay there painfully. A woman with disheveled hair, as if she had seen enough, said sympathetically to the people next to her: "Judging by his appearance, he's still in his thirties, wearing a silk cotton robe, not like someone from a poor family. To die like this in a foreign land, not even his family knows. Where is he from?"

The old man who sold morning snacks had witnessed this tragedy. He was there, telling others in a rambling manner: "This man was trying to catch the Deqing ferry. Just as it was getting light, he hurried out of the alley with his package, and his foot slipped somehow, and he fell down. But it wasn't a stroke, how could a man so young have a stroke? Someone saw it at the time, and there were other passengers who saw him lying on the ground struggling, his face turning ugly, his breath fading; who dared to help him? Someone without a name or background, if you kindly helped him home and he ended up dying, you wouldn't be able to get out of it! If he died, they would say you murdered him. He died painfully within minutes, but no one was willing to help him. This matter can only be settled by the local bailiff..." - In order to avoid getting involved, no one was willing to lend a hand to a dying passenger, leaving him to die on the road. Who can say there is any compassion in this world?

Although everyone used shallow conversation and laughter to throw at the lying corpse, there were still some kind-hearted people who found out where this man came from. In a small town, the mouth is the best news spreader. A fur trader recognized this man as his customer. The man's surname was Xia, from Deqing, and he was in the fur business. This time, he came to purchase sheepskins and earned more than a hundred dollars. Last night, he was drinking and playing cards with others. This morning, he wanted to go back to Deqing. Perhaps his family, young and old, were hoping he would bring money back for the winter, but who would have thought he would die on the road! The woman and children at home, who are working for a living, are still waiting for him with hopeful smiles. Shouldn't someone go and notify them? A fur trader's assistant went to make a long-distance phone call. The crowd of onlookers gathered even more. Someone found two reed mats to cover the man, to avoid obstructing traffic.

In the afternoon, the man's family came. Seeing this tragic scene, the woman burst into tears. The crying moved many people even more. A white-skinned coffin was placed beside him. But they still wouldn't let the body be quietly placed in the coffin. It was said that those bailiffs who were supposed to be helping to watch over the body were asking them for money to provide a written guarantee. The woman had no choice but to leave the body lying on the road, with tears in her eyes, and was forced to go to several places to beg for help!

Opening Piece "Baoyu Cries at the Spirit"

The most amorous is ultimately the most foolish. Ill-fated beauty has been said since ancient times. It is lamentable that after the beautiful girl's soul departs, spring never arrives at the Xiang River. The Prince of Joyful Red cannot exhaust his feelings, crying before the spirit to show his sincerity. Only see the grass and trees wither, the sound silent, a desolate scene everywhere. The parrot does not know the affairs of the heart, murmuring poems about burying flowers. Seeing the saddle, one must think of the horse. Seeing the object, how can one not think of the person? Sister, I call you peerless talent now has vanished. Empty left belongings before. Just want to accompany you often. Who knows all things are determined by heaven, not by man. Pitiful that you have suffered so much since childhood. Pitiful that you hold resentment and go to the underworld. Thinking back to when we played together as children. Today, ear temples worn can not. Thinking back to when we admired the moon and flowers together and wrote poetry. Today, singing wildly and writing can not. Thinking back to when our hearts were connected and we were so close. Today, shadows can not. Thinking back to you often laugh infinite good. Today, the desire to see look can not. I now often tell before the spirit. Do you know in the nether? Sorrowful. Tears falling. Like drunk like fool want soul break. This is really wealth and glory as spring dream. Life gathering and parting equal autumn cloud. To do not know jump out of trouble place. From now on cut off this unfulfilled feeling. Be a carefree worldly person.

Supplement to the Shen Bao Local Edition, Film Special

Farewell to All Readers of This Publication 237

— Bu Min

Starting tomorrow, May 1st, this publication will temporarily separate from the readers of this newspaper. Therefore, in my position as editor, I must say a few words of farewell to all readers of this newspaper, especially to those friends who have supported this publication.

The farewell words I speak contain many endless meanings. Although the Shen Bao Film Special Publication is now suspended, it can only be said to be the end of a chapter, and cannot be said to be discontinued, because we cannot judge matters solely on the basis of form. This so-called fixed position of the Film Special Publication, the one hundred and twenty square inches next to the newspaper's masthead, although temporarily eliminated in form, texts about film can still be published in other locations. Therefore, although the form is gone, the substance may still exist.

As for the reasons why the Film Special Publication is being suspended, this concerns the administration of the newspaper office, which is difficult to express in a few words here. What I can say here is that during this suspension period, we can observe whether members of society, general readers, and those related to the film industry and art feel that a publication like the Shen Bao Film Special Publication is indeed needed and whether it is beneficial to them.

Of course, there are those who express their need explicitly, and those who tacitly approve without expressing it. I personally believe that if the Film Special Publication is needed, it mostly belongs to the latter category, because for thousands of years, the teaching of "contentment in poverty and happiness in abandonment" has long told us that if there is something to eat... we eat it... if there is nothing to eat... we don't snatch it. In this way, even if the Shen Bao Film Special Publication is indeed needed (I personally do not make a definite statement here), I believe that they may not feel it is a must-read during the suspension.

Therefore, the length of the publication's suspension also depends on whether the need for such a publication is very clear and urgent.

The Shen Bao Film Special Publication has been published since November of the 21st year, which is now two and a half years. During these thirty months, this publication, under the guiding principle of "not seeking merit, but seeking no fault," has managed to contribute a little effort. On the part of the editor, I have never dared to assume the position of an advocate of film culture and art. What I have achieved is to provide readers with an interesting publication about film art, while at the same time giving them some general knowledge about film art and some life lessons learned from the lives and experiences of people in the film industry.

It is true that this publication has also published promotional texts from time to time, but these are all promotions of an obligatory nature, definitely not being used by others or having personal intentions. Furthermore, these short promotional texts are based on interest and facts. And this is very convenient in terms of editing and arrangement.

As for the editing aspect, I have received the assistance of many gentlemen during these two and a half years, especially Mr. Ling He. He has been working diligently until today. He is someone who has been with the Shen Bao Film Special Publication from beginning to end. His spirit deserves the admiration of all readers. The editor of this publication would like to express his gratitude to Mr. Ling and all the other gentlemen who have helped me.

Finally, I should apologize to the readers of this newspaper and the supporters of this publication, because during these two and a half years, I have received many letters from true friends, providing many useful suggestions. Some of these suggestions have been implemented, while others have not. But due to the editor's limited time, I have not been able to reply immediately, and I hope that everyone will understand this deeply. I have done my best to create a valuable, interesting, and just publication.

I would like to thank all of you readers for your constant support, constant encouragement.

I hope that you readers will support this newspaper with the same enthusiasm with which you support this publication, and I hope that this publication, whether in substance or even in form, will soon meet you again.

Film Reviews

Review of "Adventures of a Wanderer" 238

— You Jing

Carnival——The Grand Shanghai's Reflection——

"Adventures of a Wanderer" is about a traveling puppeteer who faces various tragedies and comedies after his wife dies of illness, all for the sake of leaving behind his orphaned child. It's a play filled with paternal love and human warmth. However, it's a pity that the playwright didn't develop the story well around this theme, often using the subplots of supporting characters to replace some of the main character's inner performances.

The life of a person who makes a living performing puppet shows is already precarious and drifting, with more sadness than joy. How could he endure the pain of his wife's death? The author overlooked the dramatic aspects and instead arranged two close friends for the protagonist Zhike: the famous pickpocket Mike as his musician and the young Daisy as his puppeteering assistant. Thus, with Mike's help, Zhike steals his beloved son from the hospital where his wife's father had placed him for adoption and flees to another location to wander. If the story had continued along this path, there would have been plenty of drama to be made between a single wanderer and his young son. However, the playwright has Zhike return with his son two years later, where he meets Daisy and others, who have become a good nanny for Zhike's blood.

Naturally, if it continues this way, the play will only develop from the romantic aspect between Zhike and Daisy, which is inevitably too monotonous. Therefore, the playwright pulls the play into a lively background. The World Centennial Celebration has opened, and in the grand occasion of various performances, there is a children's competition. Mike uses a little trick to swap the election tickets, and Zhike's child actually wins the first prize. As a result, the case is solved, the child is lost, and a fire breaks out in the amusement park, all these exciting scenes come together. In the end, Daisy saves the child, and Zhike gratefully holds a prison-themed wedding with her. After serving six months, they can finally enjoy the happiness of being a son, husband, and wife.

Such a disorganized play is inevitably dull, so it can only hope to be adjusted with lighthearted gags and intense stimulation. Here, a nurse secretly kisses Mike, who came to steal a child, due to a romantic appointment with a doctor. Mike's humorous stealing everywhere, chasing women in the amusement park and getting slapped, as well as the troupe from "selling savage heads" including fat women, Japanese people, and women with beards, and the chaotic scenes of fire and capture. Unfortunately, the excitement and fun ultimately cannot cover up the emptiness of the content. The traces of artificiality and coincidence seem to be attempts to conceal the obvious.

Director Walter Lang's overall sensitivity is commendable, but he failed to use concise and clear editing to remedy the disorganized parts. Several turbulent multi-person scenes were handled better than scenes with fewer people but more drama.

The protagonist, Li Tuo, is used to acting in fast-paced dramas with lots of action. In this "Adventures of a Wanderer," which is full of worldly flavor and requires inner performance, he works very hard, but unfortunately, he did not achieve the best results. The big-nosed Jikesen's achievement here lies not in making people laugh with humor, but in grasping the personality of the character Mike in a fairly thorough and profound way.

The actress playing Daisy has a character that is too vague in the play. It is not clear why she loves Zhike and why she can't express this point, so her performance is flat and undeveloped.

This Day Ten Years Ago 239

— Dong Lin

Ten years ago, Katharine Frances and her second husband, William Keyston, were traveling around Europe after their marriage, with no intention of entering the film industry at all.

Sally Eilers was still a red-haired country girl attending Fivers High School.

Joan Blondell and her parents traveled around in an old Ford, performing in traveling troupes.

Lupe Velez and White Balan Stainfield were still studying at a high school in Brooklyn.

Dick Powell was working as a bill collector for a telephone company in a small city and was preparing to get married.

Guy Kibbee was working as a clerk in a stock company in the western region, earning forty dollars a week, and thought there was no hope of "getting rich."

Janet Gaynor had just resigned from a bookstore in San Francisco and was trying to find an opportunity to be an extra in Hollywood.

Dolores del Río was still a social star in a Mexican city, and did not even understand a word of English.

The script for "Mother" has been sent out for re-review. The cast has not yet been decided.

Gao Lihen's new work has not yet reached the stage of publication.

Wang Bin has been promoted to director. He will write and direct a film himself.

Blockbusters such as "Mr. Wang" and "Happy Enemies" will be released in Tianjin in order.

The Tianyi authorities plan to recruit actors who can speak Mandarin in Beiping. This plan should be realized soon.

Tianyi also has a book group organization.

"The Great Hand" has become a popular song on the streets. There have been requests for sheet music from Yunnan and Xinjiang.

Film Novel

Rose of Thorns (The Devil is a Woman) (Part 2) 242

— Wen Ying

Pasqua listened to Antonio's words and knew that he was also fascinated by Kanga. He felt he should fulfill his duty as a friend, so he told Antonio everything about his relationship with Kanga, as well as Kanga's actions, to the fullest extent. After Antonio heard his words, he was filled with righteous indignation and vowed to Pasqua that after seeing her once, he would humiliate her thoroughly before ceasing all contact with her.

But Kanga's methods were truly amazing. After Antonio met her, he had already fallen deeply in love, irrevocably so, and the anger he originally felt in his heart had vanished like smoke. But strangely, Kanga also developed genuine feelings for Antonio, for the first time in her life. But her happiness was not long-lasting, because Pasqua soon learned about their affection for each other.

Although he hated Kanga, he could not bear the fact that his original position had now been taken by someone else. Although he knew Kanga's methods were despicable, his love had not completely died, but was instead stirred up by Antonio's new love, to an unstoppable degree.

He demanded a duel with Antonio, and his demand was resolutely accepted by Antonio.

That night, Kanga pleaded with Antonio, urging him to flee the country and take her with him. But Antonio said that he did not have a passport and could not cross the border.

The next morning, Pasqua and Antonio arrived at the dueling location as scheduled. Kanga also came. Her face was ashen and her body was trembling. She did not hesitate to beg Pasqua for mercy. She told him that she truly loved Antonio and begged him not to duel. But Pasqua did not say a word, and the preparations for the duel proceeded as before. When he held the gun, turned around to shoot from a distance, a kind of unfathomable, miserable smile appeared on his face. He pulled the trigger, but he deliberately fired into the sky.

Antonio, however, believed that Pasqua was going to kill him, so he aimed at Pasqua's head and fired. Pasqua did not die, but was injured in the eyes and went blind. At the same time, the police arrived. Pasqua was taken to the hospital, and Antonio was arrested because he did not escape.

Kanga, for the sake of Antonio's life, remembered to be in danger, so she went to see Governor Basquito. She used all her seductive skills to try to get him to agree to release Antonio. At the same time, she managed to get two passports, telling the governor that the two passports were for her and a cousin to go abroad. The governor also believed it to be true and did not investigate further.

Soon, the two of them had reached the border. Kanga couldn't help but feel a pang of sadness. She tightly held Antonio's arm, and her face was as pale as velvet. Antonio, on the other hand, was elated... He had gained freedom and the love of a beautiful woman, and now he was setting foot in a foreign country, like lovebirds, their joy was unparalleled. But as the train shook and was about to depart, Kanga quietly jumped down, leaving Antonio to go alone.

The train had left, and Antonio was shouting desperately, but Kanga only pointed her hand, shaking her head, her eyes filled with tears, and her heart was about to break. She knew that if she followed Antonio abroad, she would not be able to have peace of mind for a moment, nor enjoy happiness for a moment. She felt that there was only one way: ...that was to return to Pasqua's side. He needed her. She should confess all her sins to him. She decided to devote her future years to repaying her past mistakes. (The End)
