Shenbao Architectural Weekly

Essentials of the Latest Hospital Architectural Design (Part 2) 243

— Liu Jipiao

C. (Patient Department)

Wards are divided into men's, women's, children's, maternity, and newborn infant rooms. In addition, there are public wards and private wards.

(1) Public Wards - Modern wards are smaller than in the past. Each room accommodates approximately eight to twelve beds. There is now a trend to further reduce this to four to two beds. A room accommodating eight beds can measure 22 ft x 42 ft. A room accommodating two beds can measure 16 ft x 16 ft. The size of the ward is determined by the volume of space that each person should occupy, i.e., each person should occupy at least 1,000 cubic feet. A center-to-center distance of eight feet between beds is appropriate. The beds can be separated by screens. A ceiling height of 10 ft 6 in is suitable. The window should ideally be one foot wide. The windowsill should be two feet six inches from the floor, with the top edge half a foot from the ceiling. The corridor width can be eight to ten feet.

The light entering the ward should not directly face the patient's eyes. The best direction is for the head and the wall between the two windows to form a right angle.

In addition to public wards, there should also be small wards for patients with infectious diseases, and a quiet room should be set up next to them for patients who are afraid of being disturbed or who can disturb other patients. The location should be near the nursing station.

(2) Private Wards - The size and shape of private wards should be such that patients do not feel depressed when they see them. Space should be left for tables and chairs in addition to the bed, so 10 ft x 16 ft, 14 ft x 16 ft, or 12 ft x 18 ft are appropriate. A washroom and toilet should be provided nearby.

(3) Children's Wards - The upper part of the partitions in children's wards should be fitted with glass for easy supervision. The inside of the corridor should also be fitted with glass. The room should be painted with pictures for decoration to provide comfort to the children.

(4) Maternity Wards - There should be an entrance hall leading to the delivery room (at least 12 ft x 16 ft). There should be a sterilization room and a utility room. The nursery should have at least one hour of sunlight every day and good natural ventilation. In terms of area, if the maternity bed area is 30 and each child requires a space of 200 to 300 cubic feet, then the area should be 3 x 23. The temperature should be maintained at 80F. For soundproofing purposes, it is best to separate it from the corridor with a vestibule. A dining room should be set up nearby for the diet of the mothers and children. There should also be a small nursery for infants with infectious diseases.

D. (Operating Department) is usually located on the upper floors because of its abundant light. However, some are also located on the first floor, in which case large windows are used. The most important part of the operating department is the main operating room, approximately 18 ft x 24 ft, and the secondary operating room, approximately 14 ft x 16 ft. The ceiling should not be lower than 12 ft to ensure adequate space. The width of the window should be eight feet. The windowsill should be two feet six inches high, reaching directly to the ceiling. The window should have light-shielding equipment because sunlight is sometimes not allowed to enter. A strong electric light is installed on the operating table. The configuration of the light should be such that there are no shadows. The interior color is best to use gray-green ceramic tiles to protect the walls, which are then painted with light gray-green. The floor is paved with dark gray-green tiles, but the tile surface should not be too slippery. Modern operating rooms often have a student viewing area. This area is located on the upper floor of the operating room, only seven feet above the floor. There are saddles all around. Students can lean over the glass screen and look at the operating table. Their line of sight is directed in from the edge of the short wall in front of them so that people below will not notice.

Next to each operating room, there should be a sterilization room and a doctor's washroom. In addition, the attached parts include an anesthesia room, a nurses' work room, a small laboratory, a doctor's rest room, a changing room, a toilet, etc. The anesthesia room should be approximately 12 ft x 16 ft, and the walls should be set with warm colors.

Study of Building Materials (11) 244

— Zhu Zhenmu

(4) Copperization - The pure copper obtained after melting can be placed in a copperization device, with a small amount of sand and raw copper ore added, and air is injected into the liquid at a pressure of 16 pounds per square inch. Then the sulfurous substance is transformed into sulfur dioxide, and iron sulfide can also be transformed into iron oxide and combined with sand to form slag. Stop working and take out the slag. Then absorb air to remove the sulfur in the copper sulfide, and then pure copper can be obtained.

(5) Refining - Although pure copper has been obtained after copperization, it still needs to be refined. The method can use electricity. For electric refining, the electrodes can be arranged in parallel or in series. The solution used is copper sulfate and a small amount of sulfuric acid mixture. The electricity used should be low voltage and high current, and the current density should be 25 amperes per square foot of electrode. After electric refining, the copper block of the anode is oxidized into Cu, passes through the solution and adheres to the cathode, thus obtaining truly clean copper.

Section 3 Characteristics and Uses of Copper

Copper is soft and easy to stretch, and its color is slightly reddish. The maximum resistance of raw copper is 25,000 pounds per square inch. The proportional limit is 8,000 pounds per square inch, and the elongation reaches 7%. For those who use fast cooling, the maximum resistance is 40,000 pounds per square inch, and the elongation is 3%. The use of copper in the construction industry, such as electric wires, window decorations, or the manufacture of various alloys, is widely used.

Chapter 7 Aluminum

Section 1 Overview of Aluminum

Looking at the history of aluminum, before 1850, it was still a rare metal mineral, only enough for museum exhibitions. It was not until 1889 that there was a market for trading. It was first discovered in 1825 by Osterd. At that time, the value was very expensive, such as one hundred and twenty or thirty gold yuan per pound. Nowadays, it only costs one or two jiao of gold, because the traces of aluminum are all over the earth. According to scientists' exploration, about 8% of the earth's crust is aluminum, while iron is only 5%, so the reserves of aluminum are richer than those of pig iron. However, aluminum does not have a simple mineral vein, and is mostly mixed with other minerals, so it must be smelted to obtain aluminum. The most common mineral vein is aluminum oxide, called Bauxite in the West. The impurities it contains include iron oxide sand silicon, etc., which should be purified during smelting.

Section 2 Smelting of Aluminum

The smelting of aluminum is usually done with electricity in order to meet the needs of large-scale production and supply, and to reduce costs. Moreover, without electricity, aluminum cannot be extracted purely. The commonly used aluminum smelting methods include the Bayer method and the Hall method. They are described separately below. Architectural Jargon (10) 245

— Mei Zhenhuan

Regarding the usage on the construction site:

Green Bean Sand - In general, reinforced concrete construction projects, the components of cement, yellow sand, and gravel are indispensable. Therefore, in the era when the modern construction industry is booming, the output of cement, yellow sand, and gravel occupies the most important position. But what exactly is this green bean sand (Gravel)? It is a kind of small stone chip, with properties similar to fly ash. However, its use is not needed for mixing cement for large materials and pillars, etc., because it is not easily subjected to tensile and compressive forces. However, it is extremely important in places such as window sills or chimney caps (Channel Cap).

Sun Step! The arrangement of a staircase sometimes becomes several sections of curves in the middle due to the position. In the curved areas, the treads (Step) are difficult to inlay as a whole. They are probably made into long triangles. These long triangular treads are called sun steps (Winding).

Air Vent - An air vent is a kind of ventilation equipment, mostly small square or rectangular iron bars left around the outside wall of the floor joist wall. This is an air vent (Ventilator). However, ordinary street houses rarely use air vents. In more elaborate small foreign-style houses, there must be floor joists in their construction, so air vents are unavoidable.

Plumb Bob - (Plumb) A kind of thing that can be used to observe the inclination of the wall (that is, the so-called "rush" and "exemption"). The shape is like a pig's heart and liver, hanging from a line at the top. To use it, hold the upper end of the plumb line with the first thumb and second finger of your right hand, and gently press the remaining three fingers on the wall. The plumb bob itself has weight. It should be at least two or three points away from the wall. At this time, use your eyes to aim, and you can see the "rush" and "exemption" of the wall on the straightness of the line. Therefore, the use of this plumb bob should be commonly prepared by everyone on the construction site, from the supervisor to the worker.

Worker! In the construction site, whether it is a plasterer or a carpenter, all those who are working are called workers (WordMan).

Dutou! The large ends (Lining) on both sides of the Shikumen and the outer wall corners (Angle) are probably at the position of the Xurlin, and another kind of Suzhou stone or other stone is inlaid. This kind of stone is called Dutou (Jamb).

Mountain Head! There are many names for walls, most of which are divided (calculated as ordinary city houses). The one built in the front is called the front veranda wall (or front eaves wall), the one built in the back is called the back veranda wall (or back eaves wall), the one built in the stove shed is called the back shed wall, and there is also a kind of front veranda wall and back veranda wall connected to the two side walls. The upper end follows the roof to form a two-sided slope, which is called the mountain head (Jamb). Its wall body is called the gable wall (Jamb Wail).
